<Content>Noisy Hotel  We stayed at the Embassy Suites on the before and after leg of a 7 day cruise.... 2 different rooms. The views from our rooms were horrible and the hotel is a few blocks from the beach. The 8 story echoing atrium is not at all condusive to the live loud playing bands they host every Fri  Sat night. Don't stay here if you want to sleep before 12 AM because the sounds reverberate throughout the entire property. I called to complain but the night desk manager didn't seem to care that I paid over $300/nt (incl taxes). They were more sympathic to the 5 people listening to the band. Even worse, each night my wife and I scratched from what I believe were bed bugs. Yet, we didn't itch at all during our 7 day cruise. The room had an odd stench that is consistent with that of bed bug infestation. The free morning breakfasts and afternoon happy hour was nice but not at the expense of basic accommodations.

<Author>DRIzz
<Content>PreCruise Hotel - Good, not great Stayed one night at the Embassy Suites (Carolina) near the San Juan international airport prior to leaving on the Carnival Victory and a southern caribbean cruise.Traveling from California, we had to leave at 6am Pacific time and not arrive in PR via Dallas until 10pm PR time. By the time we got to the Embassy Suites, all the restaurants were closed despite the website indicating that the Outback steakhouse would be open until 2am. The manager said that only the bar was ever open that late. When I informed him of the error in the hotel's website, he seemed to care less. I would hope they would correct this information because on the cab ride to the hotel, the cabbie offered to pull into a fast food place and get my family food (two very young, starving kids plus 4 exhausted adults). Instead, I opted to trust the hotel website and it was wrong.Secondly, we arrived to a virtual Calypso concert in the hotel lobby - so loud it was hard to hear the clerk at the check in desk. Apparently at least one wedding and one 50 year wedding anniversary were being celebrated. It was mid-night. No one could tell me when the party would end. We were tired and hungry and it didnt seem that rest nor food was going to come anytime soon. This is not what I signed up for.Had to take a cab 6 blocks to a very busy Chilis for dinner. They took an hour to make 5 sandwiches. Got back to the hotel at 130am with music still blaring. still no clue when the party would end. The room was able to void out most of the noise and my 1 year old was able to fall asleep with ease. Room was typical Embassy Suites - clean and comfortable. Breakfast bar was extremely busy and hard to find a table. Buffet line for made to order breakfast was a joke so I opted for precooked eggs, bacon, etc which was just fine and very fresh. otehr choices included tropical fruits, oatmeal, cereals, breads, coffee, milk, juices as you would expect.No newspaper delivered to our room and no Hilton Honors amenities (as an honors gold member, I typically get a free snack and bottled water on check in waiting in my room). I am used to this from all other Hilton brand hotel stays - but not a deal killer by any means.There is a small casino at this hotel with slot machines and a fwe table games.Check out is at noon and this was a very very busy time for the lobby. If you can check out earlier, you will miss the busy period. Check out seemed to maximize around 11am to 1130am.One phone and one remote control in our room was broken. We reported these to front desk but no fix ever came.Overall it was a cozy night, but a bit loud and searching for food options was not fun (pizza delivery ended at midnight). The rooms were fine as was the buffet (althought busy). I'd probably stay here again if just staying one night because of value and proximity to airport - but if you are looking for a long stay in San Juan, I would opt for something closer to the beach or closer to old town. We were advised not to walk the 6 blocks at night to the Chilis restaurant by hotel employees.The description of the beach being 1.5 blocks - hmmm, those are some long blocks.If you want optimum proximity to the cruise terminal, there is a Sheraton in old town right across the street from the terminal. The Embassy Suites is about a 30 min cab ride to the cruise terminal - and costs around $30. Cab from airpor to the hotel was $25 but we suspect we overpaid even though the cab fairs are predetermined by some cab authority at the airport. I bet we had some surpluss added just because we were picked up at the aiport. This fare was based on # of people. The fare to the cruise terminal seemed to be based on distance traveled. Whatever. I was confused. I didnt particularly like Puerto Rico anyway.I'll leave a review on the Carnival Victory elsewhere. If I fail to mention it there, the cruise terminal is horrible and mismanaged. The aiport in SJ is also very undersized and not very well run.

<Author>orr333
<Content>A Nice Place for Families or Business We stayed at the Hampton Inn pre-cruise so decided to try the Embassy Suites post-cruise. This Embassy Suites is located very near Isla Verde Avenue which has many places to eat, drink and gamble. The hotel also is very near the airport (5-10 minutes max). Cab from the hotel to the airport (4 people, 5 bags) was $18.00. Cab from the Royal Caribbean pier to the Embassy for the same person/bag configuration was around $25. The hotel had flawless checkin and allowed us in earlier than the posted 4 PM checkin. The courtyard area was great. The casino is smaller but had lots of people playing. Live music was in the casino later at night. The pool was very pretty and had a nice hottub area as well but we did not have time to use it.We used laundry onsite which was adequate. The health club is fairly small for a business hotel but had a couple of each of the most popular machines.The rooms have an older decor but were clean and well maintained. It seems that the bathroom in ours was newer except for the floor tile. Again, still very nice and clean.The beds are not yet converted to the Embassy Suites style in the states as they still have bedspreads. I much prefer beds with duvet covers that get washed every stay vs bedspreads.The free business center was great as well as the wireless internet available throughout the hotel. It was nice to get back in touch with people after being on the cruise.Noting that San Juan is a very expensive place, the manager's reception with snacks and drinks held even on the Sunday night we were there was a nice freebie. The cooked to order omelets and other hot breakfast items were all very good and add to the value of this hotel. The breakfast / reception area is large at this Embassy allowing ample seating for many guests. Given the choice for our next stay, we'd choose this over the Hampton Inn even though it is slightly more expensive.

I truly can not say enough good things about this hotel and it's great value and staff!!Yea the furniture is a little dated but who cares?? <Author>winksgal
<Content>Good, Not Great My husband and I stayed at this Embassy Oct. 22-28. We received a AAA rate of $152.99 plus tax, plus the hotels resort tax of 12% made the room around $180. Also, self parking in the parking garage was $14 a day. The hotel is located within a mile of the airport, but we were never bothered by plane noise. He was there on business, and I was there for pleasure. The resort tax allows you to make free local calls and use the wifi from your suite. Note: the wifi was sometimes weak on the 7th floor and not powerful enough to use in the bedroom part of the suite. Our room was clean, but the carpet needs to be replaced, and the furniture in the bedroom was nicked. A paint job was also needed in our suite. The king bed in our suite was comfortable, except for stiff pillows. The rate includes breakfast which includes made to order omelets or eggs (tip is not accepted like Embassy's in America); bad pancakes; so-so french toast; fruit; cereal; toast/bagels; juices; coffee; yogurts. Also included is the Manager's Reception Happy Hour from 5:30-7:30 nightly. You can get two drinks (or a double) per person at a time, but there is no limit to how many times you go back. There's one beer on tap, wines, and mid level alcohol. We tipped a dollar at each trip. Some people don't tip at all. Popcorn, a mix of chips, and pop were available as well. Service from the staff was not consistent. Some of the younger employees were not as helpful as the more mature ones. The pool is clean, huge and lovely. There's a pool bar, but it was never open. After numerous people asked for drink and food service, a staffer came out and took orders. Drinks were delivered promptly, but the food took over an hour. Except for a few smoking suites, this is a non-smoking hotel, as most establishments in Puerto Rico.. even the casinos. But, you can smoke outside at the pool, or out front of the hotel. There are ash trays and benches set up in the front, but no ashtrays by the pool. Most people just put their cigarettes out on the ground. Towels are available for free at the pool, and you can also take them to the beach which is a good 2 blocks away. We didn't make it to the beach but heard it was very nice. There's a self laundry room on the main level which requires $1.75 to wash and $1.50 for a 30 minute dry. The front desk will exchange bills for quarters and sell you a small ziploc bag full of powder detergent for $2.14.Note: There is a gift shop, but it's under renovation at this point.We ordered room service 4 times and the food was pretty good. Sometimes not as hot as we'd like, but we'd use the microwave in our suite to warm the food. If you like burgers, order them well-done, or they'll come out pretty rare. I recommend the french onion soup. Pizza Hut and Domino's delivers to the hotel, but you have to go to the lobby to retrieve it. We didn't order from Pizza Hut, but Domino's pizza was good and reasonable. Inside the hotel is an Outback Steakhouse. It's as good as any I've been to, but more expensive. It's open for dinner only Sunday - Friday, and opens for lunch on Saturdays. We ate lunch at Lupi's (near by) which was expensive and just so-so. Be careful ordering pop, no free refills. There are two ATMS in the hotel. There was no fee involved except for what your bank charges. You can also cash a check up to $100 a day at the front desk. Be prepared for your check being denied by the security check company they use. One of our checks was approved, the other denied. The casino is on the small side. Lots of slots including penny slots. Two blackjack tables, a 3 card poker table, and 2 roulette tables in which one was always very busy, and rarely did they open the 2nd even if there were people standing around wanting to play. I think the casino opens at 11 am and closes at 4 am. There was entertainment in the bar/casino area Fri-Sun nights. Good, but most songs were popular hits only in PR. Taxi's are always available but pricey, and you can pay for valet parking for $20 day. There's a free business office to use the internet (2 computers) and free use of the printer. There's a grocery store and other shops a block away. Ponderosa is also close by. There's also plenty of hotels in the area within walking distance that have casinos. The Intercontinental has beautiful grounds, a good casino and a Japanese steakhouse that we heard was very good. All in all, I'd give this hotel 3 stars. Feel free to contact me with any questions.

<Author>3dawgnight
<Content>Great Stay; Near the Airport I was in San Juan on business. The room was clean and comfortable. The toilet backed up on my second day there, but I reported it on my way out in the morning, and it was repaired before I returned in the evening. Parking is expensive ($14/day), but it's a covered parking deck, which is nice considering the heat. There's a very good complimentary hot breakfast every morning, including an omellete bar, as well as a manager's reception every night where guests get two complementary drinks. The drive to the airport is less than five minutes, but I didn't hear any overhead air traffic while I was inside the hotel.This was my second stay at the Embassy Suites San Juan, and it will be my first choice the next time I find myself in Puerto Rico.

<Content>Spotty service (Disclaimer: I previously wrote a pretty scathing review just after our honeymoon, but thought that wasn鈥檛 fair as I was still in the heat of emotion, so I have let time mellow me out鈥?We booked this hotel for our honeymoon. My husband and I are not really the pampered sort鈥e usually are able to go along and have a great time, despite slightly negative reviews (i.e. budget hotels in Italy). However, possibly the negative reviews regarding this hotel should be heeded. Thinking that this is a Hilton-owned, we figured we couldn鈥檛 be too bad off. We even booked our stay and the accompanying flight off of Hilton.com鈥檚 vacation package leg. But once we got to the hotel, they seemed to have cancelled our reservation because they rudely told me that we were a 鈥渘o-show鈥?(we had a late flight and it ended up being slightly delayed). First off, it showed that we already prepaid for our stay so it shouldn鈥檛 have mattered when we showed up. Anyhow, we were dead tired and we just needed to crash first, so we needed the room. Since they had cancelled us before finally getting a manager to reinstate us, all they had available were smoking rooms. Fatigue set in and we couldn鈥檛 argue, so we took it, but we told them that we needed to switch rooms after others checked out. They said it wasn鈥檛 a problem, which they kept to their word, and later that afternoon before we left, we stopped by the front desk to change keys and they moved our luggage into the new room for us. When we came back, they left a fruit plate and a bottle of red wine along with a note apologizing for our inconvenience, which was nice. The lay out of the suite in general was nice, with a living area with a pull out sleeper couch, dining table, mini fridge and microwave, bar sink. The bedroom was a good size for walking around in without bumping into furniture. Bathrooms were standard. The servers brought alcohol around as long as you tip (make sure you tip each time a dollar or so or they seem to disappear). They had a masseuse cabana available for massages poolside which I鈥檓 disappointed that I didn鈥檛 get a chance to try. The woman who took our order at the bar was very rude, basically ignoring us when we first got there. She could鈥檝e written down our order but instead, she forgot it and had to yell for us to repeat it once she got to the register. Ugh. By the time we ate our sandwiches which were grilled, they were lukewarm. We were extremely disappointed. She really ruined our afternoon. We ended up calling the general manager (the number on the comment card in the room) and got through and voiced our disappointment. I didn鈥檛 want to do it all trip, but I finally pulled the honeymoon card and told him that I had thought that after having my wedding at a fabulous Hilton and enjoying fantastic service, I should be able to expect having Hilton hospitality on my honeymoon as well. The general manager was very apologetic and stated to us that he will consider possibly retraining some of his staff. He asked if there was anything he could comp us on, but we told him that we just sincerely wanted to voice our opinion. I鈥檇 like to add though, that it the general manager did make us feel like he cared about how our stay was going, which meant a lot to us. So our general conclusion with this Embassy Suites? (which disappointed my Puerto Rican husband immensely) Unfortunately, at a few of the places that we went to, we got treated worse than our neighborhood Applebee鈥檚.

<Content>Nice Place for the Family We just returned from a four-night stay at the Embassy Suites - San Juan.The good: friendly and helpful staff, free cook-to-order breakfast, a nightly manager's reception featuring free cocktails, nice pool area and a small but fun casino.Located within the hotel is the Outback Restaurant. <Author>fool4jesus
<Content>Generally nice hotel The Good: the Embassy Suites Isla Verde is just like a thousand other Embassy Suites hotels. That is to say, with a nice center atrium, good breakfast, etc. It also has a small casino (if you're interested in that sort of thing, which I am not). The pool area is rather large, with a nice waterfall for the kids to play in. People complain about airplane noise because the hotel is right next to the airport, but honestly the only time I ever heard planes was sitting at the pool. Inside the hotel, you'd never know they were there.It is also an easy walk to the beach, where you can rent 2 chairs and an umbrella for $18. The attendants were reasonably courteous (it helps to speak Spanish though) and asked when we left if we were coming back. Another good feature about the location is that it is easily accessible to both Old San Juan and the eastern beach areas such as Fajardo. You must do the Fajardo bio bay tour - see my review of Laguna Grande - and it's about 1:15 drive. If you stayed in Old San Juan, it would be considerably longer, especially with traffic. The Carolina/Isla Verde area is nicely situated in the middle.One of the closest restaurants, which I cannot recommend highly enough, is the tiny Mi Casita that's right on the way to the beach. They have wonderful food, and excellent prices. It's very small but pleasant. The waiters speak English but with the busboys etc. it helps to be able to speak to them in Spanish. Order the mofongo: my wife had chicken and I had fried pork. The fried pork was rather dry, but between the sauce that comes with the mofongo and a good local Medalla beer, it is fine. The Metropol is another nearby restaurant with good local food, although we did not go there.The Bad: Not really bad, but the hotel does not really have much in the way of local feel. You could be at any other Embassy Suites hotel, and it would be just about the same. I think some of the smaller hotels in the area have much more of a Caribbean feel to them. We were only there for two days pre-cruise, but if you are there longer you may want more of a local experience at another hotel. Also, although the rooms were nice, for the high price I expected them to be a bit cleaner than they were. This seems to be an endemic problem with hotels in the area, however: and my guess is that the Embassy Suites is about as clean as you're going to get. My wife is a clean freak and she was happy with it.Bottom line, a nice hotel, good location.  
<Date>Jul 7, 2008

<Author>AZJOHN1
<Content>everything ship shape After reading so many horror stories on other San Juan hotels, I booked the Embassy Suites for the first few nights with the plan to check out some other (cheaper, closer to town) places after I landed. This Embassy Suites is right near the airport. I did not hear airplane noise. Everything here worked perfectly and was clean and ready for me. The hotel is beautiful and well maintained. There was horrific noise in the 8-story atrium most nights, either from the local band at the bar or the large banquet parties booked every night. BUT...the living room of the suite acted as a buffer, and when I went into the bedroom with the door shut, I couldn't hear a thing. The internet access was free, but when I logged on the first time it said I would be charged $10 per day. (I was not charged, just confused.)This neighborhood is listed as Carolina, but the locals call it Isla Verde after the great beach that is 2 blocks away. There is a bus (A5) that runs all the way down the coast into Old San Juan for 75 cents, but the service is slow and erratic. It goes through 2 housing projects, which might scare some people, but I felt safe. If you are not going to take the bus, taxis are expensive. Most people say you should rent a car in San Juan, but the drivers don't follow right-of-way rules, and I'm glad I did not. Parking in all of San Juan and Isla Verde is a nightmare, and the valet at the hotel was $20. If you just want to relax and go to the beach/pool every day, this place would be great. The management pays attention to details here, so you can relax. It's far from cultural attractions and real local neighborhoods.

<Author>kathy/baits
<Content>They thought of everything My two friends and I(50 something) chose this hotel for a girlfriend getaway and it was perfect for our needs.We arrived on Friday night and getting a taxi from the airport was very easy and quick.My one and only complaint is the room we reserved and reconfirmed the day before was not available. We reserved a room with two doubles, but they said the only thing available for that night was one king. They had a big party in the lobby and the only way they could accomodate them was to give them our room for the night. One of my friends planned on sleeping on the sofa anyway, so we agreed .They did comp the extra person fee as our original reservation was for two and later turned out to be three. We thought that was fair.The next day around 2 they moved all our stuff, we didn't have to wait around, and just stopped at the desk to exchange keys.The staff were all friendly and at least twice a day someone would ask if everything was ok with our room.One day we forgot the do not disturb sign on the door all day and there was a message under the door saying what time the maid was there and if we needed anything like clean towels, don't hesitate to call. I really like the layout of these suites. There's quite a space between bedroom and living room and a tv in both rooms, so especially travelling with friends who might be on different clocks, you don't have to tip toe around for fear of waking someone up. There's a frig,microwave,coffeemaker,coffee ,tea and I brought some paper plates and plastic cutlery that really came in handy with leftovers.There's a large grocery store around the corner, so we kept the ice bucket full and had a lot of drinks and snacks in our own little place. A standard room wouldn't have been nearly so comfortable.The beds were very comfortable and the powerful shower was heaven, expecially after a day of walking around in that heat. I read a review saying the pool was cold,well,not anymore. We thought it was perfect. By July, it'll probably be too warm. This Puerto Rican sun is hot,hot,hot! There always is a breeze tho, so it doesn't seem as hot as other places I've been in May.We thought the breakfast in the morning was a huge savings and very good. The first day I skipped the omelettes and just had scrambled eggs, but don't do that. You pick all your own ingredients and put it in a bowl, then wait about 2 minutes and yumm. There's also bacon, sausage, potatoes, fruit, pastries and more I've forgotten. Really a nice way to start the day.The manager's reception at night was nice, but not worth a trip back to the hotel if you're doing something else. They serve only Medalla beer, their mixed drinks are quite weak, and surprisingly enough I liked the wine the best. The chardonnay was actually quite good.Another convenience here was free internet in the lobby(3screens). There were quite a few businessmen when we were there, so I only had a little wait a couple times. I imagine when there's more kids in the summer, that might be a different story. I think there's also free service in rooms, but I didn't check into that.The biggest complaint I've read about this hotel is that it's not on the beach. I guess if you want to spend all day on the beach, that would be a consideration. We only spent an hour or two each day so the block and a half walk was no inconvenience to us.After a long tiring day that pool was so nice and never a problem finding a chair at anytime.Again, that might change in the summer. The area around the hotel has lots of restaurants from American chains to cheap authentic to posh and upscale and you can walk to all of them,Im not a fan of chain restaurants, but the Outback in the hotel was actually quite good. It's about $20.00 for a cab to OSJ and the rain forest is about 45 minutes away and a definite must see.When you add it all up, this is a great location and a great value. We would definitely return.

<Author>kj1130
<Content>Great Value Just came back from Puerto Rico and thought I would share our experience. If you are looking for a good value, the Embassy Suites is it. This hotel is moderately sized and moderately priced and was a great value.It is located near the airport which was convenient, there was a little noise from the airport but minimal. I had a hard time deciding on this hotel vs. others that were on the beach, I'm glad I picked the Embassy Suites. The beach is about two blocks away, the ES lets you use their towels. You can also rent chiars to lay on (about $4 bucks a piece) You are on the beach with local folks and those who paid to stay on the beach, so overall, for us, we felt we got the better deal.There was free breakfast every morning (omelets, pancakes, eggs, bacon, sausage, etc.) and the manager's reception for drinks every night from 5:30-7:30. You get about 3 drinks during that time and snacks if you so choose. I expected the manager's reception to be a mad house, but it was very organized. If you go, go after 6. Folks begin to line up at 5:30, if you wait a little while you will have lttle to no wait.Customer service was excellent. Everyone was friendly and helpful. Often times we were thanked for staying there. We ordered towels and they came within 10 minutes. Ten minutes later we received a call ensuring that we received the towels. It was great.We booked this hotel for $199 p/n. I'm glad that we did, by the time the additional fees are charged (it is cited on ES website) we paid $239 p/n. When researching hotels, I noticed that all of them charge these extra fees, so be sure to consider those additional fees when booking.I visited Old San Juan one day, it would have been $40 r/t in a cab, but instead I walked across the way to the Holiday Inn. They had a Dollar Rent A Car. Without taxes and insurance it was about $25 p/d, however I did have to pay for Parking in Old San Juan, so if you do rent a car, make it worth your time to have one.Overall Puerto Rico was great, it's well traveled in Isla Verde, but the city is beautiful.

<Content>Best of a bad situation My husband and I stayed here for two nights under not the best circumstances. We had to leave our cruise ship before it sailed due to a personal emergency. However, we had a pleasant stay until we could get a flight home. The included breakfast and cocktail social included in the price of the room was a definite plus. The atrium surroundings were lovely. Our suite had a separate bedroom and living room with tv's in both. The bed was very comfortable as were the pillows and linens. The rooms were very clean and included refrigerator, microwave, and coffee maker. An Outback Steakhouse was conveniently located in the atrium lobby which was open for dinner until late in the evening for late arrivals. The pool area was very nice and it was an easy two block walk to the beach. The hotel has its own small casino which was closed due to renovation while we were there. There is a business center in the lobby with computers available, free internet access and free printing. This hotel is very close to the airport, but we were not bothered by the sound of planes overhead. It would be a pleasant place to stay for a night before or after a cruise.

<Author>ccor22
<Content>Pleasant Surprise We stayed at the Embassy Suites February 21st-February 25th 2008. Travelers consisted of three couples ranging from ages 28-38. I read many reviews as I do every time I travel, some good some not so good. I must say that we were pleasantly surprised. I realize that it may bother some people that it is so close to the airport, but it really did not affect us. We never lost any sleep over that or the music in the atrium. The 2 room suite was decent and very spacious. The buffet breakfast ( which is included) was also very good. We especially liked the fact that they make cooked to order eggs/omelettes. The 2 hour nightly manager's free happy hour was also a nice bonus considering the fact that you are staying at a hotel so they overprice the cocktails. It is a good idea to go to the supermarket and pick up your own beverages. You will save considerably. I am used to all-inclusive so it was tough for me to see that they were charging $5.00 for a beer. I am by no means cheap, just pratical. Also, I read reviews that stated the beach was about a ten minute walk??? The walk is about 5 minutes, possibly under. We went to the beach several times after laying by the pool which was extremely cold. The pool was our only disappointment. It was nice to look at and that's about it. I spent most of my time in the hot tub. There are many places to eat outside the hotel. If you like to walk you will find pleanty on the way. Fortunately, I traveled with people who know the island so we were able to hop in the car and go to different locations which is a huge plus. Also, the casino which is open until 4 A.M. is pretty small, but we did not have a problem with that. I believe we make our own vacations what they are ie. fun, romantic,quiet etc. It is a great hotel for the value. We would certainly stay there again in the future. As a matter of fact, we just booked a trip for April at another Embassy Suites in a different part of PR.

<Content>Convenient pre-cruise stay We stayed here three nights precruise. Great location 鈥?close to the airport and close enough to the port. Just a block and a half away is the main street with Burger King, Walgreens, and other fast food type restaurants. A block and a half away is the beach. We weren鈥檛 there for the beach and just walked over to check it out. To me, it certainly wasn鈥檛 the beautiful Caribbean beach you might expect. We didn鈥檛 use the pool but it looked nice but small.I would stay here again for a short stay but would never select this place as a land based vacation resort. By the way, we hired a private driver for two days through Countryside Tours. This was worth every penny. We got to see so much of the real Puerto Rico plus the tourist sites of Arecibo, Ponce, and El Yunque. The Fajardo area has beautiful beaches and resorts and I would look into that area if I were to return to Puerto Rico for a land vacation.

<Author>Divehpu
<Content>Great Hotel Near the Airport As many reviewers have written, this is a nice hotel near the airport. The pool is great for kids and the beach is a short walk from the hotel. <Author>blondzai
<Content>Handy, Clean and Nice Big Rooms The hotel is literally right beside the airport landing strip and beside the freeway, yet you can't hear these noises from your room. The casino is located in the atrium and the noise from the live music filtered up to the rooms, but the great thing about the Embassy Suites is that you can close the door to your separate bedroom and you can't hear a thing. I thought it was neat to sit at the very spacious and well conceived pool and literally watch the planes coming down. The pool's waterfall, for the most part filters out the plane noise. There were enough chaise lounges for everyone who came to the pool (and it was full) and you can get a massage and other spa services poolside.The food at the Outback located in the hotel was terrific and the service that we received from the Embassy staff was great, especially the day manager, Bo. Overall, great location with clean rooms, good service, good food , conveniently located by the airport and other good restaurants, blocks away from the beach and for sightseeing into Old San Juan. I understand the taxi fares from this area to be a little high to go to Old San Juan and would recommend renting a car for the $40 a day which would also allow you access to the Rain Forest and the Caves. Parking rates at the Embassy are $14 and $20 for self and valet parking, respectively.

<Author>GoHokies07
<Content>Embassy Suites a good stay. We were traveling with an 8 year old, a 10 year old and two 22 year olds so for us the choice of Embassy suites was due to that you could fit 6 people in a suite with two double beds and a pull out couch. Very pricey - paid 209 one night, 259 another night and 309 for the weekend night. Weird but long story. Even at the 200 + per night stay it was worth it to not have to pay for two seperate rooms and everyone ate breakfast free. The free cocktail 2 hours was also enjoyed by all, as they also had sodas, virgin drinks and popcorn for the kids. The kids loved the pool. It was an easy walk to the beach. Rooms were clean. Lobby was clean and well taken care of. Eating in San Juan with little ones is difficult if you are trying to get a bit of the local flavor. We are not fans of eating at fast food joints, there are PLENTY of these if that is your thing. We did find a good place that served local dishes withing walking distance. Mi Casita. The kids all found something they liked. Don't go to any restraunt in Puerto Rico hungry as the food takes a while and in the case of Mi Casita - take a sweater. Old San Juan is a short drive from the Embassy Suites but you can rent a car from car rentals near by or take a taxi. Expensive Vallet service, plus extra 14 dollars a day to park. We also went to El Yunque on our own instead of a tour. Very easy to do. Great snack bar in the main information area - kid friendly food. The hotel is VERY close to the airport. A 15 dollar taxi ride for 6 people and 8 pieces of luggage. The front desk was very helpful in getting toothbrushes ect to the room. Had our lost luggage waiting for us when we woke up in the morning. Very nice people. Pricey for us but worth it.

I gave up on getting a second one after she walked by our table and ignored us and my empty glass the 3rd time (and I'm a VERY patient person). Casino was incredibly small and looked like part of it was under renovation. Suite and breakfast were usual for Embassy Suites...lots of room in the room and hit-or-miss food at the buffett (it was really busy and they had trouble replenishing the food to keep up). My husband bought toiletries in the hotel gift shop and was overcharged by $30 ($85 vs. $55 that it should have been), which he didn't realize until we were back home--seems the clerk there was operating on less sleep than we were.To be fair, the pool area looked nice and the bellstaff were very understanding and helpful. The other person behind the counter was very nice and promptly had toiletries sent to our room when I requested it.We are both easy going and very polite people and didn't expect 5-star treatment from this hotel, just common courtesy and respect (especially when paying hotel prices for drinks). We stayed at the Marriott Stellaris after the cruise and had a much better experience.

<Content>Double Check the Fine Print We have stayed at this hotel before because it is very close to the San Juan airport and we were only going to be there for under 10 hours. I booked a Net Direct Rate through the hotel site because it had the lowest rate. The rate was $260.39 USD, plus $28.64 for 11% hotel tax. The total rate charged immediately was $289.03. We checked in late in the evening and the desk clerk said everything was paid in full, but wanted to run my credit card through in case we had any incidental charges for the restaurant, etc. I asked him if the room was paid for in advance and he said yes, I did not owe anything. We checked out at 6 AM to rush to the airport, and were presented with an additional fee of 9% of the total. Of course, we paid it, it was under $30, but I think they should mention it on their website. I would have booked the hotel through someone else to avoid the fee. We book all of our trips online and we have never had a prepaid hotel add charges at checkout. The location for the airport is great. The decor is modern. The beds were comfortable. I also will not book directly through Embassy Suites site again.

<Author>Lukafoo74
<Content>No complaints, nice pool, but nothing that stands out as great My boyfriend and I stayed at the Embassy Suites for five nights in early December. We chose the Embassy Suites based on a combination of Trip Advisor reviews, the price, the location and the pool and hot tub. Overall, I can't say that we were unhappy with our stay, but we probably would stay somewhere else if we visited Puerto Rico again. We booked through the Hilton website and were quoted $170 per night before taxes, fees, parking etc. After taxes, fees, parking we ended up paying about $220 per night. I knew about the additional expenses in advance, so I wasn't surprised, it just starts to add up. Overall, we found travel in Puerto Rico to fairly expensive vs. the value. Most of the hotels seem to charge extra for parking ($14 per day) and include a 10% per day service charge.The best features of the Embassy Suites are the pool, the breakfast buffet, the manager's reception, the in-room fridge and the free wireless internet. Most of the staff was helpful, and we didn't have any trouble with the maid service. The lobby and courtyard were pretty and overall the hotel seemed to be clean and well-maintained. Our room was a nice size and it was nice to have the two separate areas, but the location of our room wasn't the best. The pool is pretty large, although the water is a little chilly. The hot tub is nice for a hotel. Also, the pool and hot tub were not super crowded when we were there.While in Puerto Rico, we found that the minimum that we spent for a meal was $30, the average was about $50 to $60 and the high end was over $100. Drinks run from about $4 to $5 for a beer to $10 for mixed drinks. That said the breakfast buffet and manager's reception, although not the best, probably saved us some money. Things to be improved upon are the on-site dining options and I wasn't thrilled with the location. We did not try either restaurant on-site, one of which is an Outback Steakhouse, but I heard from others that the food and service were not good. We also didn't spend any time at the casino, but it looked kind of small.The location of the hotel is ok. It is near the airport and some other nicer hotels (El San Juan and the Intercontinental). There is a beach a few blocks away. Carolina/Isla Verde feels fairly suburban and it seemed like there were a lot of business travelers in our hotel. There is a strip that you can walk along that has a few restaurants and there is good access to the highway. Old San Juan is about a 15 minute drive from the hotel. We went to the San Juan Hotel and Casino on a Saturday night and had a lot of fun, there seemed to be a lot of local people there.During my initial search, I couldn't find a hotel in our price range (under $200) in Old San Juan that had the amenities that we were looking for (pool and hot tub). Plus, once we saw Old San Juan, it seems like it might have been pretty noisy to stay in a hotel there. Our other choice was the Marriott, which was slightly more expensive and in Ocean Park. The area around the Marriott was under construction, but the Marriott itself looked nice, is closer to Old San Juan and had some more upscale shopping.We probably would have had a different experience if we stayed in another area, next time if we return we would probably try the Marriott. Again, not a bad experience, just nothing that stands out as great. We also went inside the Holiday Inn, the Intercontinental, El San Juan and El Convento. All were nice, El San Juan seemed to be the most happening, but didn鈥檛 seem as nice as the Intercontinental. El Convento was in a good location and really pretty.Background info on us, we are mid-thirties and take 2 to 3 trips per year. Last December we went to Cancun and the year before we went to Miami and Key West.

<Author>jomia
<Content>Watch out for the surcharge! 2 December 2007I spent three nights in this hotel in early November, 2007. I travel a great deal, several months a year. In my experience this hotel is marginally satisfactory but uninspiring. The room size is a bit cramped but adequate. The decor is rather tired and the furnishings eclectic. The personnel do their jobs - but they do not go much beyond that.The most annoying aspect of this hotel is the 9% surcharge that is imposed on your bill. You are not advised of this surcharge until you arrive at the hotel. When you sign in, you must also sign a statement accepting this charge. At best, the hotel can be accused of false advertising. At worst it is a form of extortion since your only alternative is to take your bags and look for another hotel. The hotel states that the surcharge is to cover local phone calls and web access. I do not use the phone since I have a cell. As for web access, at most hotels it is free or charged at a rate that is considerably less than the cost of the surcharge. (Incidentally, the connection speed is quite slow.) The hotel, although located near the airport, does not even provide shuttle service!Considering these factors and the relatively high room rates and remote location, you would do better looking elsewhere.

<Content>Loved the Embassy experience I read a lot of good reviews about the Embassy and decided to risk it after reading that construction was going on at the El San Juan. Room 416 which we were assigned was a very pleasant surprise. We did not expect a suite with two televisions. Everything was impeccable, the staff helpful and courteous. We still patronized the casino at the El San Juan which is 5 mins away because it is bigger than the casino at the Embassy. My husband said it best, on a scale of 1 to 5, I give them a 10.

<Author>Steffie326
<Content>Nice Place Hubby, myself and another couple stayed here from Oct 3 - Oct 8. The rooms were very nice - suites- with a separate living room area. Very confortable beds, roomy bathroom and accomodating service. The pool area was enjoyable, free internet access, nice bar / lounge area and the lobby was tropical with an open atrium  lots of foliage. Free full breakfast available, including ready to order omelettes / eggs, bacon, sausage, potatoes, bagels, toast, cereals, oatmeal / farina, coffee, juices, etc, etc. More than enough to start the day. Free evening reception which amounted to free drinks for guests from 5:30pm - 7pm. Two blocks walking distance from the beach and other restaurants  hotels. We enjoy walking and after a full dinner, welcomed the opportunity to stroll along Isla Verde Blvd to visit other hotels. We went to two local restaurants: Barrachina  Mi Casita. Both were within walking distance and very flavorful - check them out! Also, we asked them for a recommendation for a local bakery. They gave us directions to Espana Bakery on Calle Marginal Villamar. This bakery is awesome! Only 5 minute drive from the hotel and they had everything from pastries to sandwiches to quiches to hot meals and even liquor. Delicious! We went there the day we were leaving and picked up sandwiches to eat on the airplane. The other passengers were jealous!Down sides - they do not have an airport shuttle. The front desk said that they are not allowed to have it??? Small casino - okay for a novice, but not sure if real players would be satisfied. Daily parking fee for guests ($10 / day). You would think they wouldn't charge guests for parking. An added hotel fee of 9% (or something like that). They attribute this to providing free internet access, free local phone service and other services. Just be aware of this. Not sure if other hotels have started charging the same fee, but the Embassy does. Regardless, we got a great package deal through Orbitz.Over all, service was great. We enjoyed it, and would stay there again.

<Author>reneet39
<Content>Loved the Embassy My husband and I just returned from five days at the Embassy Suites. Service was great. The bed was very comfortable. The hotel is in a great location, not far from the strip if you are interested in having easy access to night life, as well as local resturants. It is cost effective to rent a car. It will pay for itself, by saving you from taxi trips which can cost up to $15.00/per person, as well as from tours which can cost $25.00/pp and up. The complimentary made to order breakfast was great as well as the manager's cocktail hour every evening. They made any drink you requested. Although there was a casino in the hotel, we did not hear the noise, which is great. The facilities were always clean, and staff was good. There is an outback in the restuarant for convenience. Try Mi Casita, Barrachina and Yuqi's. These are all great local restuarants.

<Author>InRebuttal2u
<Content>On the way down The hotel is located in Isla Verde, in the Caroline district, which is a great spot. There are restaurants nearby and a grocery store (all within walking distance), and it's only a couple of blocks from the beach. The Outback restaurant in the hotel is great. The casino is small, but if nickel slots are your goal, it'll do. Its downfalls, however, are too numerous to overcome the great location. First, my visit was not as a tourist, but as a business traveler over an extended stay. My employer selected the hotel, not me. My employer also paid the bill, not me. That said, had I selected a hotel and paid the bill, I would have been nothing but disappointed with my choice, and the cost.The hotel is in a slow decline. 1) I opened a drawer at the sink, and it fell apart as it came out. Leaving it on the counter got it fixed prior to my return from a meeting. 2) Like many hotels I've stayed at, there are two banks of elevators. Here, there's a bank of elevators and across the way a single elevator. The single elevator is extremely slow. The 2nd floor and ground buttons stopped working. I was on the 2nd floor, and just started using the stairs. 3) The in-room 'fridge was missing a foot, which meant when you opened the door it tilted toward the missing foot and all items shifted.4) Music from the lobby bar and special events was OUTRAGEOUSLY loud! It was impossible to watch television, read, or look over any documents while sitting in the front room from 8-11 at night (again, I was on business, not a tourist), and a call to the manager two nights in a row did nothing. If you have kids that go to bed early...good luck to you. Ultimately I went to the bedroom and closed the door between the rooms. That certainly took the benefit of a suite out of the picture. I might as well have been at a Super 8.5) The dresser in the bedroom smelled a little like someone had upchucked in it. I decided rather than complain once again I'd handle it by purchasing some air fresheners from the local grocery store. That made my clothes smell like someone had upchucked on them, after they had been freshly laundered. Not a good smell.6) Parking at the hotel was terrible. In the evenings there are events at the hotel and the attendees take up all of the available spaces (except on the roof, where the employees park). Cars are parked on concrete dividers, and in the lanes of travel in behind cars (which can be bothersome when you try to get your spot out of an actual space). If you park, get a space early and don't move your car or you'll be sorry.All in all, I would recommend shopping around for another hotel. If it's only for a short stay, you plan on being gone most of the time (out of the room) anyway, and the cost is what you need, then enjoy.

<Author>TravelinGatorFans
<Content>Good hotel for the money We stayed at this hotel for 2 nights after a recent cruise. As others have said, it can be tricky to find if you're driving yourself, but once you get your bearings, it's not so bad.We arrived hours before check-in, and although we couldn't get into our room, the hotel stored our baggage so we could go exploring. Once we got into our room, we weren't disappointed... It was a 2-room suite with more than enough room for us and our 6 year old daughter (who was thrilled to have her own room and tv). The room was very clean and looked pretty new. The bed had a fitted sheet on it, which I always like to see in hotels (hate how the flat ones can come off during the night). Our room overlooked the pool (and the highway, which is RIGHT next to the pool), but while I worried about noise from planes or traffic, there was NONE! The same can't be said about noise from INSIDE the hotel. Our first night there (a Sunday), there was a singer and music in the lobby that we heard plain as day in our room. The good thing was, it was over by about 9:30, and after that, all was quiet.The breakfast in the morning offered tons of choices, from omelettes to pancakes to cereal. Something for everyone. Our first morning there was very rainy, and that may have led to the REALLY long breakfast lines. It literally took us 25 minutes to get our food. Yikes! The second morning, though, there was practically no line. Go figure... It would be nice to have the breakfast open later than just 9:30. Seems kind of early for a hotel that has a lot of tourists as guests.Our only real problem with the hotel was that our room was never made up on our full day there. We'd left the hotel at around 9:30 and got back at 3. The room hadn't been touched. Went to the pool for another 2 hours; still nothing. We got a a call at around 5:30 asking if we'd like for them to make up the room for us. At that point, we figured why bother, and just asked for new towels. All in all, I'd recommend this hotel. The pool was very nice, and the staff we ran into were very pleasant. It's walking distance to the beach, is clean and bright, and a good value for the money.

<Author>Travelbudz
<Content>Just Lovely! This hotel was a little taste of paradise. I actually preferred it over the beach. My friend and I spent most of the time eating and drinking alongside the pool. Don't get me wrong--we swam as well. The lagoon is a spacious pool of 5 ft. that sits right beneath the sun and palm trees. At times, it may be frequented by a bunch of kids, as the hotel seems to attract families. The staff is extremely friendly and accommodating. We had a leak in the sink and maintenance came right up to fix it. We didn't have to wait. The rooms are spacious and clean, and the bed...the most comfortable I have ever slept on in a hotel!! I didn't want to leave the bed! The continental breakfast offers pancakes, french toast, omlettes, fruit and all types of sides. The hotel is one block away from the main strip where American fast food restaurants, Walgreens, 7-11, night clubs and other hotels are. Just a few steps further and you're right on the beach! Expedia doesn't mention the hotel service charge, so don't be surprised when you check-in and sign off on 10% extra daily. Will definiately stay again!

<Author>Cheeseshoney
<Content>GREAT STAY!! I stayed at this hotel from June 28-July 5th and I plan on going back!I stayed here with 20 family members and we loved it. Having stayed at the El San Juan down the street which is an upscale hotel, I liked this hotel much better, especially traveling with children. The suites were very spacious and very clean. We had a view of the pool which was great and although planes are landing all day long, you cannot hear the planes from your room. The breakfast every morning was a great money saver as well as the managers reception every evening with top notch liquor. Great food and great drinks.....can't beat it!!We ate at Mi Casita which I've eaten at before, the first night the food was WONDERFUL, it was true island food, but our second visit was not as good, there must have been different cooks. Also be ready for slow service at the resaurants and also read your bill before tipping as most restaurants charge 15% gratuity no matter how small the party. We also ate at Levi's at the end of the strip which had good service and food was okay. If your in the mood for fast puerto rican food at a good price, try the Pollo Tropical, also down at the end of the strip.One thing visitors to the Embassy Suites should watch out for is their final bill. The hotel charges you for a 9% hotel fee which includes local calls. Having family in Puerto Rico I did make some calls and also called down to the desk before calling to confirm they were free because of the 9%, I was still billed for each call 1.25 plus tax. So make sure to check your bill, the front desk took it off, but make sure to check and not be overcharged. There were also about 2 proms while we were there,but did not bother us at all, we were on the 4th floor and our room was over the prom area...but again no problems. The beach is 2 blocks down about 5-10 minute walk and Isla Verde Beach is beautiful. I have traveled to Loquillo Beach before but this year Isla Verde Beach was perfect. Overall this hotel was a perfect stay and I definitely plan on visiting again!

<Author>booksntravel63
<Content>Rude Staff and Dirty Dishes Await You!! My adult daughter and I stayed at the Embassy Suites in early May 2007 for one night - thank God it was only one night. The thing that I find ridiculous about the rate is they quote you one price but you will end up paying quite a bit more after they tack on all the various taxes and fees (Puerto Rico LOVES fees, fees for EVERYTHING!!!) even the valet parking added taxes and fees to their $16.00 per night (ended up costing $23.00 without a tip) The bellhop sat there looking bored while we struggled with our bags, never offering to help two ladies upon check in. We just blew it off and went to our room. The room itself was fine, okay but we were tucked away at the very back of a wing away from any sort of view that would have made the stay a little nicer. We ordered room service (again, fees fees fees + a delivery charge) and the tray was still sitting outside our room the next day when we checked out. There were room service trays outside many of the doors throughout the hotel during our stay that never moved. It was gross really. Now for the best part, the CASINO staff is really rude, be prepared. We went in to the casino to waste some time and money after a great dinner at Ruth Chris Steak House (recommended highly) and we spent about $300 on slots in the course of several hours before we were offered a drink. I had asked 5 different waitress/wait staff people where I could BUY a drink and they each told me it was someone else's responsibility. So after 2 hours we finally got our drinks and proceeded to gamble. It was my 19 year old daughter's first opportunity to gamble (gambling/drinking age in Puerto Rico is 18) so she was excited and I wanted to take a photo of her pulling the slots...mind you, I had NO idea photography was not allowed in the Casino, there were NO signs anywhere stating this and since I don't normally hang out in casinos, I did not know this was typical for casinos. Well, I took out my pocket camera and started to take a photo of my daughter. A staff member (janitor) came up and smiled at us and said in extremely broken english (I could not begin to understand what he said at all) what I *thought* was oh this is a good place for a picture, isn't it? and I smiled and said yes it is he then started waving his hands around and SCREAMED inches from my face still unintelligible but enough for me to understand this time what he was trying to get across....NO PICTURE, UNDERSTAND!!!! I was stunned and embarrassed. There was NO need to scream at me, I did not understand what he had said originally and since he was smiling when he said it, how was I to know that he was indicating I was doing something wrong. I hate being made to feel stupid, especially by the casino janitor in broken english. This obviously ruined our night. We went to the Hotel Manager and were told there was nothing he could do about it since it happened in the Casino. We went to see the Casino Manager and were told to wait for him, that he was busy. We waited (ignored) for over 40 minutes before we decided to just forget it. I can't believe we were treated so badly and paid all that money to Embassy Suites to get that sort of treatment. Just be aware if you go here, you are going to spend a bundle and may get treated like a chump!!

<Author>tpfeeney
<Content>Fantastic Girl's Weekend Getaway! Myself and three girlfriends stayed at the Embassy Suites - San Juan May 3rd through May 7th. Visiting Puerto Rico was a first for all of us, so that is why we chose to vacation in PR. And we all agree it was a great choice. The Embassy Suites worked out perfect for us. We booked 2 suites, so each of us had our own bed and only had to share a bathroom with one other person instead of 3 other people. Well worth the extra money spent. The separate living room area worked out perfect for getting ready for dinner and relaxing. The bedroom was very spacious and comfortable.The complimentary breakfasts were fine. Some food items better than others, but you can't really complain when you don't have to leave the hotel and it is included with your room. The nightly manager's cocktail party was definitely worth visiting each night. They gave you 2 drinks each time you went up and the lines moved pretty quickly. The bartenders were friendly and gave heavy pours! Always a huge plus! One thing we did learn is when ordering a hamburger from the Atrium Restaurant, make sure you order it well not medium well because ours was still raw. The pool area was great. While we were there hardly anyone used the pool, so you always had your choice of spots to lay in the sun by the pool. Although we never actually saw the pool bar open, which would have been a nice to have been able to order a cool beverage by the pool, but we survived without them. The beach is a quick 5 minute walk from the hotel. And the majority of the restaurants and bars are very close as well. We walked at night to and from the hotel and never felt unsafe in the area. (I don't condone walking around at night, because crime still does happen, but we never felt nervous.)Some of the best bars we visited were the lounges and nightclub at the El San Juan Hotel. Very fun and lively. Definitely check this place out and dress accordingly. Pretty upscale but beautiful, especially the bordello salon. Club Liquid at the Beach  Water Club Hotel was a nice place as well. It is on the rooftop. Very pretty skyline and beach view. We visited Old San Juan which was incredibly beautiful. We went one afternoon there. We all wish would have been able to spend more time exploring this area. The restaurants and bars looked like a lot of fun. I definitely come back to the Puerto Rico and the Embassy Suites. Wonderful vacation!!

<Author>ChicagoPalomas
<Content>Worth the money My mother, husband  I and our four children (6 and under) stayed at this fantastic hotel. It is pricey but the stay was worth it. The beach and a lot of restaurants  shops are in walking distance. The breakfast buffet was excellent. They even make you an omelet if you want. This hotel does get full so at times it was difficult to find seating. In the afternoons, they provide complimentary drinks and snacks. We don't drink alcohol but they provided non-alcoholic pi帽a-coladas and other fruit drinks which we all enjoyed. The hotel lobby is beautiful and the staff very attentive. We were there for two weeks and a few minimal things came up but once we addressed the staff everything was taken care of quickly. The pool is fantastic. They have a waddling pool for the little ones as well. Room service was good (plentiful and hot). My husband did try the Steakhouse in the hotel with some friends and he states the service and food were good. A negative note is that the washing machines and dryers weren't all working. Four machines were working out of 8 or 10. Several times I tried to use the machines and it didn't wash or dry well (left everything unclean/ soaking wet). For a hotel so large they should keep up with its maintenance. They did refund the money we lost. On the weekends they have live music, which is nice but when you are trying to get your toddlers and newborn to sleep it doesn't help at all. Next time we will request a higher floor level and to have a room in one of the inner hallways. We will most definitely return to stay here again. It has been the best hotel experience, in all of our visits to PR.

<Author>CRDUSA
<Content>Inconsistent and... This was our second stay at this hotel. We had a very nice room which overlooked the pool. However, I think this will probably be our last stay at this property and in San Juan in general. Hotel: The breakfast, which was so fabulous last year, has taken a step back. They used to make omelettes in omelette pans and they were great. Now, they make them on the grill, using cylinders to keep them round. Well, I ordered two, and each time the outside of the omelette came out overcooked and the inside was raw. Additionally, it was amazing how many times the cooks made mistakes as to who had ordered which omelette. It was like they had never worked at this job before. Also, the lines were very long each and every morning. The cocktail reception in the evening, always a nice plus, has also taken a step back. No longer will they make blender drinks, as in the past. Additionally, like the breakfast, the lines are very long. The pool is very nice. However, the surface outside the pool is inexplicably slippery and dangerous. I mean, who would construct a pool like that? Time and time again, I saw people, especially little children, fall. Some toddlers even fell back, banging their heads. If you have little children, you must stay on top of them and insure they don't run (very difficult to do with kids). I'd be willing to bet, sadly, that this pool has seen its share of serious accidents. Also, there is no lifeguard, which is a shame. The location of the hotel is not great, but we knew that going in. It is about a ten minute walk to the beach (straight ahead). On the way to the beach is mall on Avenue Isle Verde. Just be careful, when walking with small children, of the metal spikes that line the sidewalk and the entrance to the parking lot to the mall (another construction decision that I fail to understand). Staff: This is the most perplexing part of this hotel and of Puerto Rican people in general. I don't know if it's an aloofness, language miscommunication, or intelligence issue. But, the service was not very attentive, and mistakes and misinformation permeated our stay. Examples:Me: Do you have to pay for children on the bus?Front Desk: I don't know, I don't have any children; andMe: What have you heard about the Asian restaurant next door in the Holiday Inn?Front Desk: I have never eaten there; andMe: What time does the pool bar close (question asked at 3:40 pm)?Pool Bar Bartender taking my order: 3 pm; andMe: How long does it take to get to the Condado using the bus (a 3 mile trip)?Bellhop: Over one hour.Me: But, it's such a short trip.Bellhop: The bus makes lots of stops.There are many more examples. A waitress in the Outback Steakhouse (inside the hotel) was rude and incompetent. She brought the wrong order, took 20 minutes to bring our dessert, and made us wait another 20 minutes to get the check. All of this without an apology. Also, the service at the fast food restaurants in the mall is not only very slow (1/2 hour just to get some chicken at Church's), but also inept. The orders there and everywhere were wrong every time. The casino staff was also not very pleasant and unprofessional. A blackjack dealer misdealt a hand and the Pit Boss just got rid of the cards instead of making things right. No sorry or even an acknowledgment that the players were wronged. Same situation at El San Juan Hotel. The blackjack table decides to change the minimum from $10 to $25. So what do they do? Grandfather the players already gambling? Of course not. Just kick everyone off of the table!Be aware, that even though English may be an official language of the territory, and many service people allegedly speak and understand English, Spanish is what's spoken in Puerto Rico. Learn some Spanish before you go. Misc. Notes: There is an excellent supermarket called Pueblo, just a short walk from the hotel. When leaving the hotel, make a sharp right and walk along the highway exit and then make a left at the corner. Pueblo is great for stocking your fridge with drinks, lunch foods, and snacks. Why pay the high prices of the hotel? Get a small, soft cooler and you will be able to keep your drinks cold while at the pool or beach.The Asian restaurant next door at the Holiday Inn is excellent. It's a bit pricey, but the food is great and the service, unlike everywhere else, was outstanding. Also, Metropol, for authentic Puerto Rican and Cuban food, is nice. It has a kid's menu, is reasonable, and you eat among locals, which is great. While nothing fancy, it is worth a visit. Make a right on Avenue Isle Verde and walk down about 1/2 mile, just past the cock fighting arena. Conclusion: As I stated earlier, this may be our last trip to San Juan. It is an easy flight and inexpensive, which makes it attractive. But, we were in search for beauty. I've been told that Puerto Rico has some beautiful beaches. Well, those beaches do not exist in San Juan. The beach on the Condado is not nice. Isle Verde Beach, which many guidebooks say is beautiful, is not that at all. Isle Verde beach has lots of pollution in its sands. When we were there, there was an influx of seaweed. While I'm sure the seaweed isn't always present, the debris from the sand doesn't go away. The beach is mediocre because of the debris. I'm hoping that in other parts of Puerto Rico, Rincon for example, the beaches are as they are pictured and described in the guidebooks. That is why, if I come back to Puerto Rico, while I may fly into San Juan, I'm renting a car and searching for some real beauty, because the beauty is not in San Juan.  
<Date>Apr 21, 2007

<Author>Chicagojill
<Content>very satisfied Just returned from a girls' trip to Puerto Rico. We stayed for 5 nights at the Embassy Suites, as many other hotels are in renovation. With four women, it was a wise choice! The hotel is centrally located for the beach and activities of Isla Verde. Parking costs $10 a day, which is economical for the area. Cabs are also readily available for all of the sites. We were checked in early, despite arriving over an hour before official check-in time, to a good sized room. The room was very clean and serviced well each day, including special requests. We did find one roach during the stay. The front desk staff and bar staff were very friendly. The hotel has a great pool, which has music on the weekends. Unfortunately, the cocktail and food service at the pool is a bit irregular and ends at 3pm, which is disappointing. The free happy hour, standard with Embassy Suites, was quite a draw, and we had to wait in a long line for drinks. Thankfully, they were more than accomdating for two drinks when we reached the front of the line! ;-) The free breakfast is too early for vacation travelers, but we did manage to hit it one day and were very satisfied. For a smaller group, I may stay somewhere else, but with a large group, I would definitely stay again.

<Author>neuromax
<Content>Excellent Quality and friendly We recently stayed at Embassy Suites April 4-8th. It was a quick getaway during spring break for our boys, 9 and 12. We made the reservation thru the Hilton website and used a AAA discount. We decided to stay here based on various reviews and the fact that breakfast was included with the deal. I hate having to wander around in order to find food in the morning, especially with kids. It was also close to the airport so that we could get there sooner and leave later. The cab ride is fixed to various hotel zones and ours was $10.50. Check in was quick and the hotel staff were very friendly and helpful. Our room was a connecting suite with a living room in the middle. One room had a king bed, the other, two double beds for the boys. We thought about the cheaper option of putting them on the sofa bed but we're glad we didn't. The sofa bed is fairly lame and our boys likely would have been kicking each other thru the night. This way they had their own bathroom and TV. We paid $379/night plus taxes. You could stay here for less than that easily but have only one main bedroom and sleeper sofa in the living room. The beds were comfortable and the rooms were clean. The service thruout the hotel was excellent. We really didn't go to the pool much but opted for activities and the beach. The pool is decent but seemed crowed at times. The beach is two blocks away and an easy walk. We liked the beach at Isla Verde and thought it was better than Loquillo. You can rent an ubrella for $10/d and chairs for $4/d. The breakfasts were good, not great, but very convenient, with enough variety for everybody. We went early, 8am, when crowds were not too bad. There was also snacks and drinks served from 530pm to 7pm each night. The resturants in the area are decent but not great. We did not eat at the most expensive places being with the kids. We liked the idea of eating Puerto Rican food although some of the places were slightly dirty in our opinion. We ate at Metropol and Mi Casita which again were decent and inexpensive but could have been cleaner. We had sushi one night at Momoyama in the Intercontinental hotel which was good. All of the above were in walking distance from hotel. Other activities included taking a cab to El Morro which was excellent($20 cab ride each way), renting a car and going to El Yunque and Loquillo beach(pretty good), and taking the sailing and snorkeling trip with EastWinds Catamaran(kid friendly) which was excellent. The only thing that I would consider doing differently is perhaps staying closer to the east coast, such as the Westin or Las Casitas. We were scheduled to do the bio bay but were too tired after the snorkeling. I didn't want to drive back the next day, but if closer, would have considered it. Overall it was a good, quick vacation with warm weather. Certainly better that NJ which had temps in the 40's.  
<Date>Apr 12, 2007

<Author>FancyDay
<Content>Great for short family stay Our family stayed here for 2 nights after spending 6 days on Culebra Island, PR. After enjoying the spartan accommodations there, our 2 bedroom/2bath suite (plus living room) at the Embassy Suites seemed luxurious. The beds were extremely comfortable and the bath products were higher quality than you find at most chain hotels. All the staff were genuinely accommodating.The free breakfast, although not spectacular, offered lots of choices and quantity. Skip the complimentary happy hour -- the appetizers were popcorn and snack mix.The pool is great for kids. The beach is an easy five minute walk. Even though the airport is just minutes away, the noise isn't offensive outside -- and inside I never heard a thing.I can't imagine staying here unless you are with children or at a business function (even though there's a casino). And I wouldn't choose it for a Puerto Rico destination hotel. But its a great stopover for a few days on your way in or out of San Juan.

<Author>outlaw06
<Content>great trip we were at the embassy suites in isla verde from march 8-11. The hotel its self was decent.. .nothing spectacular, but no problems. We paid 359 per night... for a suite which housed 5 people easily. There were two full sized beds in the bedroom and one pullout sofa in the living roon. The breakfast buffet is a must with eggs, bacon, sausage, and all the fixins. there is even an omlette bar where you pick your own ingredients. The hotel is very close to the airport, but i didn't here one plane go by, even though i can see the planes from my room window. The cost for taxi from the airport to the hotel should be 12 bucks... unless you have 4+ people. the cost to cab it to old san juan was 20 one way. The hotel pool was good... but there was no beach that it leads onto. The hotel is about 1.5 blocks from the beach..... so no direct access from the hotel. The hotel did have a casino which i didn't use much so i can't comment on it... but drinks are free if you play at the tables for some length of time. There was an outback steakhouse in the hotel which was good to see after a very disapointing outing at a local restaurant where i tried th Mofongo.... which believe me sounds a lot better than it is. One thing that i recommend everyone to do before they leave is goto the rainforest and stop by the Bio Bay in Frajoda(sp). We went there on a boat with 16 in the group. When we first got there it wasn't much of a site.. until you get into the water....I'm not much of a swimmer, but i put on a life vest and ventured into the darkness ... the further away from the boat i got.. the more intense the glo was...it was one of the most AMAZING things that i have ever seen. Make sure you go there late at night... We didn't actually jump into the lake until about 11:00 pm. But it is a must for anyone coming to PR. They have other bio bay's around PR, but the one in Frajoda was the closest... and we were able to go there right after the rainforest. The water was said to have 4x the salt concentration as the ocean, so not much was living in the lake besides the glo organisms. A plus for you ladies... and men also is that your skin will be baby soft after you wash off the salt remains.by the way .. the photos above are pretty good representations of the hotel

<Author>AK-in-NC
<Content>A nice enough hotel This property is somewhat difficult to find if you drive there yourself. Once you get your bearings, though, it is not difficult to find at all, but traffic on Isla Verde can be overwhelming. Parking is in a garage adjacent to the property, and will cost $10/night. The room was just what you can expect from an ES property...large suite, comfortable bed, large bathroom, microwave, refridgerator. Nothing special, but nonetheless a very comfortable place to stay. There is wireless internet access (for a fee) that works very well. Breakfast is very good, and so is the managers reception, although that was very crowded. There is an Outback Steakhouse in the hotel. Otherwise, other restaurants are a 5-10 minute walk away. The beach is a 5 minute walk.The property has a large and unusually shaped pool with a seperate hot tub. Be forewarned: The hot tub is HOT!I would stay here again.

<Author>peamomma
<Content>Great hotel We recently spent 3 nights at this hotel. We were wary, since it wasn't a beachfront hotel, and we have had bad experiences with Puerto Rico hotels before (El Conquistador, in particular).We were thoroughly delighted with the hotel, the staff, the amenities, etc. The staff went out of their way to make sure that our stay was pleasant. The hotel is a typical Embassy Suites, with a 2 room suite setup (living area and bedroom). The free buffet breakfast was substantial (hot and cold foods), free happy hour each night (a variety of wine, beer, liquor), free wireless internet throughout the hotel areas (including pool), free business services (fax, internet, etc). They even have a kiosk in the lobby to print out your boarding passes. The hotel is an easy 5 minute walk to the beach.All in all, I would highly recommend this hotel for a stay in San Juan.

<Author>NJVPMan
<Content>Embassy Suites A Great Deal Stayed here for 5 nights over President's weekend at $300 a night because the hotel that we usually stay in was charging $450. a night. Convenient to airport. Noise of planes and highway nearby didn't bother us. Poolside waterfalls and music tend to mask noise. Pool area is very nice with hot tub, kiddie pool, bar with food service, tables, plenty of lounges so you can get a seat even if you don't get there until 9:00-9:30 AM. Buffet breakfast was excellent with made to order eggs, fruit, yogurt, breads, juices, meats. Manager's cocktail party every night for 2 hours with free drinks, pretzels, chips, etc. Restaurants are somewhat limited (Outback on premises and Embassy kitchen). We took taxis to Ruth's Chris Steakhouse (expensive) at Intercontinental Hotel, Il Mulino (expensive) at Ritz Carlton, The Ranch (moderate) at El San Juan Hotel. The Holiday Inn is directly across street and Asian restaurant there is reasonable priced and very good. You can save a lot of money on lunch by walking one block to small shopping center which has a Burger King, Subway, bakery, mini market, ice cream store, Ponderosa. We found the Embassy Suites to be very family oriented.One Complaint----when we went to check out, there were two taxes on our bill which came to about $50 a day additional. We had booked on their website which stated that there was only an 11% tax. They have added on a new tax since January 1, 2007 but they took this tax off our bill since we had booked before that date and brought our printout with us.

<Author>keirao
<Content>What you'd expect from a 3-star hotel Embassy Suites Hotel is an average hotel, with some nice features for the $$. I usually like to stay at more upscale resorts, but this was a last minute trip booked with friends.Pros:-This hotel is literally 5 minutes from the airport so the cab fare is about 12 dollars-Breakfast is inlcuded and they have fruit, omlettes, cereal, french toast, eggs, etc. It is also served until 10am, which is nice.-Drinks at the pool are cheap-Free cocktails from 5:30-7:30-Very close to El San Juan HotelCons:-Casino is TINY-Noise from the airport is slightly annoying while at the pool-Maid service was erratic (one day they didn't come until 6pm) and we sent them away because we all needed to shower and get ready for dinner.-Bathrooms were definitely in need of an upgrade (lots of chipped tile/grout)Overall this is a perfect place if you want an inexpenseive hotel with some free drinks. I would not stay here again unless I was on a budget. There's much more going on at the El San Juan Hotel and it's much nicer. We did overpay for this hotel since we went over MLK weekend, but it served it's purpose. Pool area was nice, drinks were great, and people were warm and friendly.

<Author>NewYorkAndrea
<Content>Wonderful customer service We just got back from a weekend at this hotel and were very impressed. In fact, we booked it because of other positive reviews we found on TripAdvisor! The staff here were very accomodating and friendly. I requested a room above the 4th floor facing the pool and they switched us right away. The hotel is a short walk to the beach and although Isla Verde doesn't have too many attractions, we found this to be a good base. Everything was clean and the breakfast buffet had a good selection.The only thing I wasn't impressed with in this area of San Juan was the high price of taxis. This obviously had nothing to do with the hotel; but I was surprised that a 5 minute drive from the airport cost us $10. A short drive to Old San Juan (about 8-10 minutes away) was $20. We tried to negotiate but were told by the hotel reception that different cabs charge different rates and that's just the way it is.Other than that, though, we had a fabulous stay!
