<Author>traveler69
<Content>Embassy suites offers good value for the price. We stayed here in December '06 for a one night pre-cruise visit.We booked online well in advance and got an excellent rate of $150.00 a night. The room was spacious and clean, the front desk personnel were friendly and accomodating, and the free extras result in a superlative value in this relatively expensive neighborhood. You can take the money you save and make a donation in the on-site casino. There is a manager's reception/ happy hour offering free drinks and snacks for 1 1/2 hours each evening and a free breakfast is also offered each day. The breakfast is served buffet-style with eggs made to order, bacon and sausage, an assortment of pastries, hot and cold cereals, bagels, muffins, breads, fruit, juices, coffee and tea. If two people had to pay for the extras independently they would surely cost as much or more than the entire cost of the room. The beach is a few short blocks away. There is a wondeful outdoor pool that was never crowded. There is also an Outback Steakhouse in the hotel and the prices are very reasonable. The Ritz-Carlton, which is just a few blocks away, offers a Friday night seafood buffet that can't be beat. It's a bit pricey but well worth the expenditure. Another excellent restaurant in the neighborhood is the Metropol; also just a few blocks away. They serve Cuban, Caribbean and Puerto Rican cuisine in a family-friendly atmosphere at reasonable prices. Taxis are readily available and when we were ready to head to the cruise pier, there were several van-size taxis waiting there which were able to accomodate our entire party and all our luggage. We will definitely stay here again as the cost is low and the value is high. Discerning travelers will appreciate the friendly service and overall value offered by this hotel.

<Author>SpecialK89
<Content>A Great Value Just returned from a family vacation/birthday celebration in PR. We stayed at the Embassy Suites for 3 nights over the Thanksgiving holiday. Many of the previous posts accurately described our stay. The rooms were VERY CLEAN, the staff was FRIENDLY and HELPFUL (Ian was great). When we requested a room with a view, we were given a suite on the 8th floor overlooking the pool, a body of water (wasn't the ocean?) and could see the mountains in the distance. Very nice. Although I prefer beach front hotels, oceanview rooms and balconies, the Embassy Suites (which doesn't have any of these) still delivered a tropical feel.The location was good; didn't mind being next to the airport. We couldn't hear the planes at all inside the hotel, but could outside at the pool. Urban dwellers won't miss a beat. We rented a car so the location was great, next to the highway and main Isla Verda drag.Foodies will not be impressed with the breakfast buffet or manager's nightly reception. Definitely quantity over quality. The buffet is reminiscent of college cafeteria food. Vegans should skip the buffet all together, unless bring your own rice/soy milk for cereal. Ask for the basic mixed drinks and you will fare well, ie., rum and coke. Also be strategic, because the lines can be very long -- which cancels out free because your time/energy is worth something, especially on vacation. Run over to the El San Juan for GREAT mixed/frozed drinks and atmosphere.Definitely a great group/family hotel when you have to accomodate various budgets.

<Author>amazingrace214
<Content>Our PR Home away from Home I've been reading reviews at least 3-4 times a week since I booked this hotel in April 2006! We stayed here from Oct. 6-8. I am extremely satisfied with my stay here and paying attention to the reviews was well worth it. It is a 3-4 min ride from the Airport. Lobby is beautiful with a rainforest atmosphere. The atrium style setting of trees and small waterfalls is very relaxing. Pool in the back is nice with a jacuzzi and kids pool. And although the highway is behind the pool, it didn't bother us at all. Its kind of hidden by all of the trees. Also, we only heard like 2 airplanes our whole stay-but after living in New York, who cares! Breakfast is just as other reviews said; satisfying with all breads, juices, tea, coffee, cereals, fruits, and regular fare, as well as made to order omelets, waffles and pancakes. Yes, definitly get there between 7:30-8:30 because after that it does get crowded-towards the end, you may not even be able to find a seat, and there are plenty of seats! We ate enough every day last until dinner. Internet is $9.95 per day, so if you need to use it, make sure you understand it will be charged to your room or credit card. Live music nightly and just a walk to a local Ponderosa, Mi Casita  the other resort/hotels on the strip, plus a grocery store. We stocked up on water and fruits. Having the fridge and microwave is a big plus. For your El Yunque tour, I HIGHLY RECOMMEND Rafael from PR 4 LESS. Ask Bo, or the other managers/staff to hook you up with him. He really enjoys taking people through the island, and if you're hungry after, he'll take you to a real authentic PR roadside stand/restaurant to eat. That was one of the greatest parts of our trip. I will definitly return to Embassy Suites. Not only are the rooms/accomodations great for the price, but it felt like coming home every night. We moved over to the Ritz Carlton after our 2 nights here and although the Ritz is beautiful, probably best for honeymoon/anniversary vacations, the atmosphere is kind of stuffy with a lot of business people. Embassy has a very relaxed feel. There are a lot of families that stay here, and it is also a spot for locals on the weekends. The staff is not afraid to talk to you, and smile at you, and for that we can't wait to go back.

<Author>LiamsMommy
<Content>It had everything we needed! Thanks to everybody who took the time to review this place. I read all of your reviews and took a lot of the advice I found here. My husband and our 3 year old son stayed at this property from October 6th - October 11th and we had a great time. We arrived way before check-in time and she said she had some rooms available but I told her that I wanted the quietest room available so my son could sleep. We were given room 722 which was in a corner overlooking the pool and the expressway. Some of the negatives that were mentioned in previous reviews are true.  Yes - The hotel is located next to the airport but we didn't hear the planes too much when we were in our room. You can hear the planes land from the pool area but it didn't bother us too much. Yes - The pool area is right next to an off-ramp of a highway but it's camoflauged by palm trees. We live in a city so we are used to the sounds of cars going by. Yes - The hotel has a salsa singer every night from 6:00pm on and the atrium amplifies the noise. We could hear her singing on the 7th floor in our sitting area but when we went into the bedroom and closed the door we couldn't hear it anymore. For the price and everything you get we were really happy with the hot and cold selections at breakfast and we LOVED the happy hour. I'm guessing that during the busy season the lines could get REALLY long but it wasn't that way for us. On two nights we got Outback Steakhouse takeout and had dinner in the bar area while enjoying the happy hour. We are not really beach people but we walked to it twice. I would say that it's a three block walk and you do have to cross one busy street but that cars will stop. The Pueblo supermarket was a five minute walk and was just like the markets at home but even nicer. As there's a mini-fridge and microwave in the room you can really stock up. A lot of reviews mentioned Mi Casita restaurant my husband liked it but I liked the Metropol restaurant more. (I think my husband liked that Mi Casita was less expensive) The pool area itself was nicely landscaped and laid out but it could have been cleaner. My son is an early riser so often we'd be down at the pool at 7:00am and there would still be debris from the previous evening still outside. That's my one gripe about the property. One day we had to wait an hour for fresh pool towels. Our family had a wonderful time and agreed that a 5 or 6 day stay was a perfect amount of time as the hotel is on the smallish side. Hope this helps! Enjoy your vacation!

<Author>sdflyer
<Content>Free Cocktails and Breakfast! The Wyndham San Juan is the perfect place to stay. Its adjacent to the airport and only 2 blocks from the beach. The hotel is clean, comfortable and features a contemporary decor. Each room has two beds plus a sofa-bed and includes a wet bar, microwave and small refrigerator. Probably the best part is the complimentary cocktail hour and complimentary breakfast.Our group of 12 people booked 3 rooms for one night prior to departing on a cruise. It was a perfect pre-departure party for us as the hotel offers a complimentary managers cocktail reception every day from 5pm to 7pm. They offer a variety of cocktails, featuring premium liquors as well as frozen drinks. They also include free chips and salsa and snack mix. The complimentary breakfast features a variety of standard breakfast foods; french toast, sausage, home fries, scrambled eggs, cereal, breads and made-to-order omelettes. The bell man was really friendly and offered numerous suggestions for good restaurants and night life. We walked one block to Mi Casita, a local restaurant in a small strip center. It featured local food at reasonable prices. The restaurant was clean, the food was well-prepared and the service was good. The hotel pool is beautiful, in a resort-style setting. On another note, I have to point out its probably best to request a room AWAY from the elevators. This floor is ceramic tile and very noisy with foot traffic. Overall this is a great hotel with a fun atmosphere in a great location.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Mmmmm...Free Breakfast! Great Hotel! My friends and I stayed at the Embassy Suites from June 26th-30th. It was great!Upon our arrival the bellmen were great and greeted us as soon as our taxi pulled up to the door. Since we were unable to check in until 4pm, we asked the bellmen where to eat and they recommended a great restaurant in walking distance called Mi Casita. Great food but long wait during lunch rush. We then walked to the beach which is only 2 blocks away and not a bad walk at all since in Puerto Rico they stop for you when you go to cross the street. The Beach was clean and gorgeous. On Isla Verde Av. you can find some bars and meet up with the local people or hop on the bus to get a cheap tour of town. Also if you want you can take the bus right into Old San Juan for just .75 versus $19.50 one way per person taxi drive. Check in was fast and easy. Rooms were cleaned very efficently and had a fridge, microwave, sink for cleaning (aka kitchenette). Great room with King size bed and sofa bed. Hotel provided a great breakfast in the morning that was so filling it kept us full well into mid-day. The Pool was great well maintained and staffed. There is also a massage table at the pool and the prices are rather cheap. This was a great hotel and believe me I've stayed in my share of crap traps. Definitely would recommend.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hotel nice but has issues We stayed here on a Sat night last June. It is about 1/2 mile and 10 minute taxi ride from the San Juan airport.First off I will mention that the hotel is nice and very clean. It has an attractive lobby and pool (you are near the airport but the noise of landing jets really isn't an issue). However this hotel is not without problems.The hotel does offer free internet access (as mentioned on their website) and there are three free interent kiosks near the check in desk. However, at least one of them was always out of order and the other two were constantly being used. My biggest complaint with the hotel is their handling of crowds. As mentioned we stayed there on a Saturday evening and the hotel was extremely crowded. The receptionist informed us that Saturdays are always busy because the pre-cruise crowd. (Apparently, a good number of customers stay in this hotel one night prior to their sailing date.)While the managers reception and cooked to order breakfast have always been some of the best things about the Embassy Suites we've stayed at - these are poorly handled at this one.First off the manager's reception. This hotel has a rule that there is a 2 drink maximum per bar visit. This is a problem if you have small children and your spouse has to stay with them while you wait in line for the drinks. The bar tender told me that I could come back for additional drinks, but the line was long and the wait was about 20 minutes. Also, the drinks are served in small palstic cups which don't tend to last very long. I think that, with additional bar tenders and a little more efficiency (larger cups??) the wait time could be drastically reduced.The same thing happened at breakfast. Very long lines (especailly if you wanted cooked to order foods). The wait was again about 20 minutes and finding a place to eat was a challenge.Finally, we asked for late check out on Sunday morning. Being an Hilton Honors member I've never been denied this request. However, this time I was. After having to prod for a reason why this request wasn't honored, the management finally told me that they had another large group checking in and needed to get all of the rooms ready. They did offer to store my luggage but we needed to do laundry so that wasn't much help.We tend to stay at Embassy Suites when we travel. While I might go back to this one, it was the most disappointing of all of the Embassy Suites properties that we've stayed at.

<Content>Awesome! We wound up at the Embassy Suites after we found out the hotel we were originally booked in was doing construction on their property. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Just back-Definitely planning to return Just returned from a 4 day stay and already planning to return. The hotel's common areas-the lobby, pool etc. are lovely and well appointed. The rooms, while nothing spectacular to look at, are spacious, clean and comfortable. As other reviews stated the breakfast and daily manager's reception were abundant. The staff was curteous and friendly. They responded to requests for things like a glass of ice and bandaids very propmtly. We had absolutely no problems with unpleasant smells or excessive noise. There was also a small casino that had a nightly bingo game with a $100 prize as well the usual table games and slots. Although the hotel has both a restaurant and an Outback on premises there are many places to eat in the immediate vacinity. There is a very wide range of restaurants from fast food to American casual dining chains, to more expensive restaurants as well as local cuisine (try both the Metropol and Mi Casita for native fare). The hotel is a short walk from the beach and the neighborhood seemed both safe and busy.  One day we took the local bus to Old San Juan and another day we rented a car for a trip to the rainforrest and Bacarardi Distillery. Speaking of car rentals-we bypassed the national chains and rented from a cheaper local place called Charlie's in walking distance of the hotel Worked out great-picked the car up on our last day and dropped it off that night. They took us to the airport in a van. Overall-great time-can't wait to go back.

<Author>Brian_Schoppe
<Content>OK hotel for short stay in San Juan We stayed at the Embassy Suites San Juan from March 29-31 on our way back from St. Kitts. From the San Juan Airport, it is about an $11 taxi ride to the hotel. We were greeted by a Hilton representative trying out the new Kiosk check-in, but we were unable to use this service as I was using points to pay for the stay. Check-in was quick and we were up to our room. Prior to my stay I went in and updated my Diamond profile on their website so that I would get bottled water, pretzels and a candy bar. None of this was in the room when we arrived. It was latter brought up by an attendant, but only the water, some mint Milanos, upgraded soaps, and a robe. Upon walking into the room we were greeted by a very strong smell (believe it was room 419). I thought it smelled like someone鈥檚 breather after drinking beer heavily. My wife thought it was nail polish remover. After about 15 minutes in this room we couldn鈥檛 stand it any longer. I went down to the front desk and complain. We were moved to another room on the seventh floor. This room still had a small smell, but not as bad. Also, the water, pretzels, and candy bar were already in the room, but I assume they were meant for another HHonors member.The rooms were well appointed and typical of an Embassy Suites. The front room had a fridge and microwave. Embassy has just upgraded to their new Serta mattresses, which are much better than some of the old hard ones that I have slept on at some of their other hotels (Chicago and Houston). Both the front room and bedroom had their own TVs.Both rooms we had were off in the corners. We never had any problems with noise in this hotel. I was particular amazed that our second room seemed to be 100 yards from the end of the runway at the airport, but we were never bother by noise from the planes or cars that ran on the highway near the hotel.The pool was exactly like described in previous post. The back of the pool is the embankment to a highway. You would hardly notice it down there. Plus, I ran into the same problem with the hot tub. We couldn鈥檛 find any switch to turn it on. I asked the lady who was handing out towels and she told me that it wasn鈥檛 broke but all it did was to put out hot water. No jets like a regular hot tub. I felt lied to by this explanation. However, there was also a bar, a kids pool, and large pool in the area. There was a really nice waterfall into the pool too.We enjoyed both the evening reception and breakfast. The evening reception had the custom assortment of beverages. They even had machines for those icy type alcoholic drinks such as margaritas and daiquiris. I especially enjoyed the Carlsberg on tap. Thought this was unusual for Puerto Rico, but good beer. They even had Nachos/Salsa, popcorn and a snack Mix too. Breakfast was pretty typical for an Embassy Suites. I had my typical ham and cheese omelet. We really appreciated the assortment of fresh fruit too.Took the advice of a past post and rented from Charlie Cars. Was less than a 5-10 minute walk from the hotel. We were able to drive out to El Yunque in about 45 minutes. Driving in San Juan was much like we are used to here in Chicago, if not better. Just watch out for rush hour as backups are common. Renting a car allowed us to easily get in and out of Old San Juan without the $20 each way fare.We stayed away from the Casino. I felt I had better ways of spending my money on vacation. It is loud if you are in the atrium. You can hear the sound of the machines and singer billowing out into the atrium. The place was packed on the Thursday night before we left.The one thing I really liked about this hotel was in the entrance there was a small business area. They had about three computer setup on a Kiosk so you can surf the internet. This allowed us to check our email for any notices from the airline before leaving for home.One last note as a warning. The walk from the hotel to beach is not a short one. You have to walk one large city block north past the Holiday Inn and another building to get to Isla Verde. Once across Isla Verde you have to walk down an alley between two large resorts to get to beach. You certainly can鈥檛 hear the waves from the Embassy.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A fantastic hotel! Our family returned from our stay in Puerto Rico last week. We would highly recommend this particular hotel. The staff was friendly and very accommodating to all our needs. The rooms were spotless with extremely comfortable beds,pillows and linens. The bathrooms have large, plush towels. You don't have to fight with the shower fixtures to get more than a trickle of hot water...the shower is like being at home. The atrium is lovely...a very tropical feel. We were there with a lot of family members and there was plenty of open areas to get together and meet comfortably. The pool area was beautiful and refreshing with lots of new lounge chairs and tables. There was always enough chairs for our group (and we had a lot of people in our group)...you never had to try and find available lounges. Breakfast was terrific...always hot and fresh and delicious. The manager's reception was always fun. They have a nice selection of mixed tropical drinks and decent snacks. Music is playing most of the time and it gives the feeling of being in a very happy and fun place. If there was one drawback, I would have to say it was the proximity of the airport to the hotel while you are sitting by the pool. That's the only time we noticed the planes and you will definitely notice the planes. Other than that, this hotel is the best and we would highly recommend staying here.

<Content>Don't do it! This is the third stay that I have had in a three month period. Although the rooms are adequate, and the breakfast is good, beware the downfalls. The casino operates illegally-rules are not posted and vary on a dealer to dealer basis. Take a close look and you will note ALL of the casino tactics that strengthen the hotel's advantage. If that doesn't convince you, take a look at the cashier's line (or lack thereof).This is not the norm at other casinos in San Juan. For Honors members, forget the daily papers, bottled water and other snacks that are the norm at other Embassy Suites.There is no elevator in the parking garage so there is a very good chance that you'll be carrying your luggage up and down 5 flights of stairs. There's an daily internet charge and a daily parking charge.I was pleased with this hotel on my first stay here, but I have thus learned that the Puerto Rico Marriott chain supercedes the Hilton chain in all categories.

<Author>MarcoOttawa
<Content>Excellent Value for Money Located one and half block from the Isla Verde beach (very clean) and next to a Pueblo grocery store. Excellent value for money. We got a suite on the seventh floor consisting of a living-dining area, small microwave, coffee maker, fridge and wet bar as well as a great bedroom with a very comfortable king sized bed. The hotel has a lovely atrium and a superb pool with a waterfall and hot tub. They provide a free hot breakfast buffet including cooked to order eggs, omelettes, or pancakes. In the afternoon they have a two-hour manager鈥檚 party with a free open bar. There is also an Outback Steakhouse on the premises. The hotel has a small gym and a coin laundry. The only thing that needs improvement is the room safe. It operates with a key that is inconvenient and requires an $85 deposit. Overall, it is an excellent hotel if you do not absolutely need to be inches from the beach.

<Author>smartypants01
<Content>Good hotel - here are some tips for your stay We stayed at the Embassy Suites San Juan on Jan 12 to Jan 16th. Overall we really enjoyed our stay, and felt we got more than our money's worth. Here are some of the tips I have for anyone considering a stay here:Location in regards to the beach: The location is the tradeoff for the lower price you pay. It is two block to the beach. This is not bad, even for our family traveling with two younger children. We got quite good at packing our bags full so that we didn't forget anything and have to trek back to the hotel. They do rent lounge chairs and umbrellas at the Isla Verde/Carolina beach - $4 for chairs and $11 for umbrellas if I recall correctly. Just make sure to bring towels down to the beach with you (we snagged towels from the pool area and then returned them at the end of the day)The pool: We never heard any traffic from the road that ran behind the pool. We also sat out at the pool each night with our drinks and the traffic was never loud, nor did we have any trouble with the airport noise. Only negative was that the hot tub was broken while we were there. It was hot but no bubbles.Rooms: The key here is to know that some of the rooms are renovated and some are not. Obviously the renovated rooms are better. While we were there the hotel had finished the 7th and 8th floors and were working on the 6th. My suggestion is to ask for the highest floor possible. Also, we never had any problem with airplane noise in our room, nor with the music from the lobby. Again, location may be the key. We were on the 8th floor facing downtown/Old San Juan (overlooking the parking ramp).Breakfast and Manager's Reception: To us, these were the two best reasons to stay at this hotel. The breafast is excellent. They had make to order eggs (fried, omelets, etc), sausage, bacon, fruit, cereal, juice - you name it - and it is free. However, the best deal is the Manager's Reception each evening. From 5:30 to 7:30 they offer free drinks and snacks. You can get two drinks per person at a time, and you can return as many times as you want. The snacks were tortilla chips and salsa, pretzels, and popcorn. I especially enjoyed the strawberry daiquiris! Restaurants: We tried the Outback Steakhouse in the hotel and it was as good as any Outback we've ever eaten at. Yes, the line can be long but if you tell the hostess you are staying at the hotel they usually seat you immediately. We ate there on both a Thursay and a Saturday night and did not wait either night to be seated. Make sure to bring in one of your free drink from the Managers Reception (they always let us do this) and save the money on drinks. The location of the hotel is great as far as local restaurants go. There is just about every fast food chain within two blocks (KFC, Pizza Hut, Taco Bell, Wendys) We also tried Metropol and had the best dinner of our stay, and it only average $15 per person without drinks. There is also a large Peublo grocery store one block away that has all the necessities. Take advantage and stock the room fridge with soda and water - prices at the grocery store seemed to be about the same as mainland groceries.Taxis: We did not rent a car and instead took taxis everywhere. It was about $12 each way for 4 of us to get to and from the airport. It was about $22 each way to get to get to Old San Juan. Overall we really enjoyed our stay and would stay here again. We felt that for the price it was an excellent deal.

The beds are fine, the sofa bed is a bit uncomfortable and for one night was acceptable. The breakfasts were fine. Great coffee. The nightly manager party was fun with fruity drinks, and standard junk food of chips, pretzels, party mix and popcorn.The pool was lovely, I can't figure out what people were complaining about. I didn't see any missing tiles and I made a point of searching it out. One traveler said the pool area looked like a hurricane hit it. I can't figure that out either it was simply beautiful. Yes, you can hear the planes either taking off or landing depending on the direction of the wind. After awhile you get use to the sound and you don't notice the aircraft noise. The sounds of the kids screaming and yelling drown the noise out. I don't mind the sound of the kids, I simply put on my headphones and listen to music. It's not as bad as previous reviews write and I consider myself very sensitive to unnecessary noise. The beach is exactly 3 blocks away. One long block and two short. If you have very young kids, this might pose a logistical problem because you need to carry your towels/junk and hold onto kids. I have kids 14, 12,9, so it was no problem. Yes,one of the streets is a highly trafficed street and there is no traffic light. But if you enter the crosswalk the cars did stop for us. No, I wouldn't let the kids do this by themselves. I just don't trust them or the drivers. We walked to the beach and went banana boating which can be found in front of the ESJ hotel. At the same time other kids are on the beach and my kids made instant friends. This worked out well for us. The beach is public and you can rent the chairs for $3-$4 per chair depending where you stop. In front of the ESJ hotel the chairs are $3. This place is good for a short stay and the hotel is designed for business travelers. As we saw mostly flight attendants and business people. If you like the hustle and bustle of San Juan this a decent place. If you are looking for a peaceful surrounding and limited night life you should stay a resort such as the Hyatt in Dorado.The hotel staff is very accomodating and helpful.

<Author>PRB-SantaBarbara
<Content>Under construction! Wait until done! or try Hampton Inn We thought the hotel looked pretty (atrium courtyard and pool areas)and the happy hour was fun, breakfast good.However, when we arrived they were doing some kind of work on the tile in the lobby, with jack-hammering noise that was awful. It started up again the next morning early too.We'd reserved a room with a king sized bed, non-smoking, and were told that's what we were being sent to, but after tipping the bell-boy, we discovered we'd been deposited at a room with 2 double beds instead. We called and were told we could come back in an hour and a half  a room would be ready. When we got back they had us in a room that had just had new carpet installed that day, and boy did it stink! I felt like I could hardly breathe, and had to prop our door open. Luckily, the next day the smell had pretty much gone. But there were no windows you could open to remove the smell. And to make matters worse, the thermostat was not adjustable. It was 65 degrees in the room when we got there (a shock after the delightful 78-81 degrees approximently of outdoors), and when we tried to jack it up to 76 degrees (by lowering the air conditioning) it would not budge above 71 degrees. I had to wear a sweater in my room! They sent an engineer but he couldn't fix it. Our phones didn't work either, but he was able to fix one of the two. It was nice having a safe in the room, but you have to go downstairs  ask for a key, rather than just assigning a combination like some.... And if you forget to turn it in when you check out, it costs you $85. Has a small refrigerator, coffee maker  microwave. Only coffee cups though, no other dishes. The noise at night from the band is loud, even as late as midnight or after. The band did play nice music though, but it would be hard with people trying to get their kids to sleep! The sofabed was the lumpiest  most uncomfortable one my son has ever slept on, and he has slept on many. Our bed was fine, but the spread smelled (or was it the drapes nearby) like stale cigarettes, even though it was a nonsmoking room. It was a nice beach about 2 blocks away, but not good for snorkeling or sailing: too rough of water. The Holiday Inn next door rented us a (Dollar Rent a Car) car for $38/day plus gas, but is only open something like 8 or 9 to 5pm,  no one else can give you any info. The map they give you is painfully inadequate for finding your way to El Yunque rain forest. Many turnoffs say an intersection is coming up, but when you get there, it's labeled with a different highway number. Or no number. And there are lots of highways that you won't even find on the map! It's really a challenge. Took over an hour to get to  from the rainforest due to minor getting lost episodes. It's worth going to however. The water at the falls was supposedly cold but people were still going in. Holiday Inn has a nice restaurant or two next door,and no waiting. The Outback in the Embassy Suites was good, but more money and a longer wait by far. There was a pool bar, but no one seemed to man it so it wasn't used. We had to leave to catch a plane at 5:30am but were able to grab a piece of fruit and yoghurts to take with us for breakfast despite them not yet being open for breakfast. Had muffins or something available too. Bring a nightlight because the bathroom is dark at night. I'd reserved a room for $305 per night online, but at checkout they were charging me $359, so I had to try to go online in the business center to print out my confirmation to prove my rate. They ended up honoring the $305. I think next time I might try the Hampton Inn  Suites a couple of blocks further down the street for only $215 or $220 instead for the quieter atmosphere. I saw the outside  it looked better than its pictures, but didn't get to see the pool or anything. It had a buffet breakfast included (Embassy had same but with cook-to-order so you could order pancakes or eggs over easy)and Hampton didn't have a happy hour I don't think. But a lot cheaper, and people seem to review it well. Embassy's casino seemed a bit dreary. When you walk into the Embassy you are hit with cold air and a stale cigaretty smell. Ugh. Holiday Inn is even colder to walk into! Incredibly cold!!! The bus for 75 cents each requires quarters, not a $1 bill and 2 quarters for 2 people, to get to Old Town San Juan. It's the last stop, by the way, at the bus terminal, where you get off. El Morro is very cool to explore, and the city itself is clean and interesting architecture. The free trolleys loop around. You press a yellow bar between the windows to signal you want to stop. No where to rent small sailboats in the whole area!

<Author>pointpetre
<Content>I'd stay there again A friend and I stayed here October 27 to 29. It is an excellent hotel. The atrium is very impressive. The elevator design is geometric/industrial rather than opulent, but they are good elevators with glass wall views as one ascends to the rooms. The suites had aging, slightly dowdy furnishings, but the rooms were quite comfortable and spacious. The shower-tub could use a clothesline, but that is a minor quibble. The happy hour is a pleasant plus with very good drinks. The breakfast is also very good. My friend, Dick, enjoyed the casino and found the rules for blackjack highly favorable in part because of the ability to surrender. He was up $100+ after two nights.The wonderful pool is by a freeway, but it is largely screened by dense palms and the waterfall provides white noise to hush the traffic.The staff bends over backward to provide top-notch service. The fitness center is small, but adequate and a nice retreat.It is a straight two block walk to the magnificent Isla Verde beach. It is a one block walk to reasonable shops and a variety of restaurants. The Carolina/Isla Verde area is a very nice area.We rented a car at the adjacent Holiday Inn (Less than $38 total plus $14.75 for gas). I found the other drivers to be laid back and cortez/simpatico. We drove all over the city and old San Juan. Dick could not walk much. We drove to El Yunque and as far up as we could go by car and thoroughly enjoyed the trip.It is a very short taxi ride to the airport.

<Author>CALosAngeles
<Content>Breakfast  My family and I stayed at the Embassy on August 25-27 before we left on our cruise. There were positives and negatives. I'll start with the positives: FREE DRINKS! Need I say more? The Manager's Evening Reception is held every night in the main lobby. Each guest is entitled to free drinks and snacks (nachos and popcorn). Also, breakfast is complimentary and we were able to bring it up to our room. All you can eat  drink! The location of the hotel is very close to the airport. We paid $16.00 for a taxi to take all five of us to the hotel. The beach is about two blocks away and there are many restaurants nearby. You can find both American and traditional Puerto Rican food within walking distance. Isla Verde is known as a tourist spot and there are many hotels very close by. (I would recommend the Wyndam. Very nice and classy.) The Embassy has a lively atmostphere and has a salsa band that plays into the late evening. The casino is much smaller than I anticipated though. There is an Outback Steakhouse located inside the lobby area. We noticed many many locals dining there. The pool area is excellent and relaxing. There were, however, a couple of negatives about the Embassy. The hotel has an open atrium where the rooms are located on the sides. Because of the lay out, you could hear the band playing all night long. Also, the rooms had a musty smell to them. Other than that, the value was worth the price. If you want to stay in Old San Juan (about 20 minutes away) definitely stay at El Convento. La Fortaleza is within walking distance. Definitely visit El Yunke, but be prepared to walk and get some exercise. Go to Vieques or Culebra if you have the opportunity. I loved Puerto Rico  Reggaeton!  
<Date>Sep 8, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Overall satisfied I stayed at the Embassy suites with my family. I was overall satisfied with our stay there. The staff was very helpful and the room was kept clean. Initially I was put off by the fact that our room had lots of ANTS. The staff was quick to move us to a different suite when we complained about the infestation. So I wasn't a happy camper when we first arrived. I also couldn't believe that a suite which would sleep 4 of us only had 4 drawers and a tiny closet. The drawers were small. But you know what? by the evening of our first day there we forgot all about that other stuff and enjoyed the managers reception-which is free drinks and snacks. The hotel is also conveniently located off the main road which has many souvenir shops,restaurants and a small supermarket. The best place to get puerto rican food inexpensively is La Casita which is in the shopping center near the hotel. I've also stayed at the Intercontinental hotel in the past. These two hotels are 2 that I would recomment. The advantage the Intercontinental Hotel has is that it is right on the beach. The beach is about 2 blocks from the Embassy Suites and easily accessible off the main road . Again overall I was a satisfied guest.

<Author>sassymama
<Content>o.k. stay As usual before I book a hotel I visit Trip advisor and meticulously read all the reviews. Unfortunately my visit wasn't anywhere near perfect. I traveled over the memorial day weekend with my husband and 3 small children. We booked our reservations ahead of time and requested a 2 bedroom suite. The hotel was sold out so when we arrived at 3:45 for a 4:00pm check in we were dissapointed that they did not have the 2 double bed suite we selected. Instead they told us they would put us in a king with a pull out sofa. The woman at the desk who claimed to be the manager offered me nothing else except the possibility of getting a roll away bed. After threatening to contact the corporate office she finally offered to reduce my rate by 15%. Secondly there were two nights where they ran out of clean room towels and offered to send up beach towels. Then they ran out of beach towels. The food ant the outback was ok but very very slow. The pool was beautiful and my kids loved it. The beach was about 3 blocks away you had to cross a very busy street. The hotel is a stones throw away from a major freeway and 10 minutes from the airport neither one was much of a problem except for the occasional noise by the pool. The free breakfast was below average the first day and o.k the second day. The managers reception did offer plenty of drinks alcoholic and non. But the snacks were the same every day. Trail mix, popcorn and chips/salsa. The band was very loud and echoed througout the atrium for as late as 2am atleast. The casino is one room with a hand full of slots and maybe some tables in the back (I didn't have the interest). The front desk did their jobs but were not overly accomodating. Food trays were left in the hall and the maids missed cleaning our room one day. The hotel was very clean the rooms were o.k. Not realy a kitchenette just a microwave and fridge. The lobby was very clean. But I consistently found cups and plates that were supposedly clean (old food and hair on them). Maybe I picked a bad weekend but I will not be anxious to return.

<Author>hotchildinthecity
<Content>Great Place to Stay I was in Puerto Rico from April 20 to April 24th. I booked this trip last minute so my choices in hotels were a little limited but I'm happy I stayed at Embassy Suites. The major perk of this hotel are the rooms. You can't beat the luxury of a full two room suite. The second room comes with a work/dining table, sofa and another tv with NYC channels and a kitchen area with microwave, sink and refridgerator. This hotel also has a free breakfast buffet with made to order pancakes and eggs. There is also a happy hr with live music from 5:30 - 7:30. very nice! there were light snacks and unlimited drinks for kids and adults. Theyalso have a small business center with 3 internet ready computers. This is not a beachfront hotel so if you're really set on staying right on the beach and walking back and forth to your hotel, this might not be for you. I went to the beach but it was not the main part of my trip. It's an easy 5 minute (2 blocks) walk. Embassy's pool area is very big and they have shady spots too. I loved their hot tub which is a little secluded from the main pool area. While you're out, you might hear a plane or two, since the airport is near. It is not deafening, so don't let that keep you from staying here. Once you're in the room, you don't hear it at all. We rented a car from holiday inn (next door and on the way to the beach) for about $49 and we got a mustang convertable since they didn't have any other cars left. renting a car is a good idea bc you can drive along the coast and see other areas. Be careful when you're on the road. PR drivers are a little rough.After we gave the car back, we took advantage of the bus (25cents) and took the A5 to Old San Juan. The fort is a must see bc the views are just fantastic. The buses run until 9pm.Embassy's casino is nice but a little small. You can use 5cents here so I was a fan. and i think players get free drinks. There is also live music playing from 6ish on. It wasn't so loud that I oculd hear it in my room. I stayed on the 7th floor. Also shopping is tax free. They have a pretty American mall. We hit this up on a rainy day. My only gripe about the hotel is that the concierge wasnt always there during her hours and it's hard to find a parking space in the garage bc so many people come for the casino and outback steakhouse (which is inside the hotel).

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great place to stay I just got back from five days at the Embassy Suites in San Juan. Everything about the hotel is excellent. The rooms were spacious and clean and perfect for four girls. We loved the daily breakfast and happy hour each night. The selection at both was amazing. The drinks they make during the cocktail reception are strong. You can get two at a time and go back as many times as you want. I'm hooked on Pina Coladas. The pool area is fantastic. It's a large, lagoon-style pool with palm trees and flowering bushes. The pool and hot tub were both extremely clean. There are lounge chairs at the pool that come with a canopy for those that want to get some shade. The location is perfect. It is only a short 10-minute walk to the beach. The beach is wide and you can rent chairs for $3 or umbrellas for $10. The water was crystal clear and the surf was calm. We took a 15-minute walk to a nearby restaurant, Metropol. The food is a mix of Puerto Rican and Cuban. We really enjoyed the local flavor. There is also a Pueblo supermarket nearby. Be sure to stop there and buy coffee to take home. It was much cheaper than at the airport or other tourist shops.To get to other areas within San Juan, you can walk towards the beach and pick up the bus. We took several rides to Old San Juan for just a quarter each. Taxis are faster but you can't beat the price of the bus. You can take the A5 bus into Old San Juan and then catch the ferry to Catano to visit the Bacardi Rum Factory. I would recommend it highly. The ferry is only 50 cents each way and the factory is free with two free drinks included. Don't miss El Morro, the 500-year-old fort at the tip of Old San Juan. The views are stunning.Also, don't miss the rainforest, El Yunque. We rented a car at the Holiday Inn next to the Embassy Suites for $30 per day. We drove to the rainforest, hiked to La Mina falls, and swam underneath it. It was a super hike and the water was refreshing.Another must see is the bioluminescent bay at Fajardo. It's one of the most amazing things you'll ever see. We went on a kayaking tour with Eco Action Tours. I had never kayaked before and it was so much fun. They take you out in 2 and 3-person kayaks through a mangrove swamp and into a lagoon filled with the glowing plankton. The highlight of the trip is getting into the lagoon and swimming. The faster you swim, the brighter the plankton glows. I've never seen anything like it. Be sure you try it, you won't regret it. It costs $40 for a two-hour adventure. Totally worth it. Since El Yunque and the Biobay at Fajardo are so close to each other, you can rent a car and see both in one day. This was much cheaper than the excursions offered by the hotel and you could customize what you wanted to see and where to stop.Have a great time in Puerto Rico, there's a lot to do.  
<Date>Apr 20, 2005

<Author>ohiowanderer
<Content>Good place to stay We (a family of five) stayed from March 19 to March 27. The hotel was fine. The airport was close but you can't hear the planes from the rooms. The pool was lovely. There is a nice exercise room and having the laundry was a bonus when traveling with a family. The teenagers loved the breakfast buffet. Having a suite was a real bonus for a family - nice to be able to close the door to the bedroom if some want to sleep earlier or later. The neighborhood was safe. I felt fine letting my teenagers walk to the beach or the shops during the day.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent Value Stayed from 3/29 to 4/1The hotel is in excellent condition (like new). The lobby is spacious and nicely landscaped. The level of cleanliness everywhere in the hotel was remarkable. Service was extremely efficient, very courteous and helpful. Always a smiling face.The included free breakfast was very good, but I strongly suggest ordering an omelet (very good) rather than taking the eggs from the steam table (well, they _are_ eggs on a steam table). The made-to-order pancakes were also very good. There was also this white gooey stuff that my wife thought was grits and I though was cream of wheat. Most of the local guests were scooping it up like crazy, so I broke down and tried it. It was really excellent, but I still didn't know what it was. I finally asked, and it turned out to be oatmeal, but I certainly didn't recognize it as such. It was very good, but it was loaded with sugar (which, I suppose, is why it was so good). Avoid if dieting. There is also an assortment of cold cereal, freesh fruit and the usual bagels, muffins, toast, etc. Several juices, yogurt, American and Puerto rican coffee, etc. The Puerto Rican coffee in the rooms is better than that served at breakfast.The included nightly manager's cocktail reception si also excellent. Pretty much anything you want in the way of drinks. Alcohol was not scarce in them! Contrary to other reports, there are no hot hors d'ouerves (at least not during the week), but they are available for a modest price. Corn chips witn salsa and cheese, Chex mix, and pop corn are included. Have drinks served in plastic if you want to drink by the pool, which is also very nicely landscaped.The room was in excellent condition and smelled fresh. No great views from any side, near as I could tell. Bands play till 9 or 10, or sometimes 11 just outside the casino, so if you go to bed early, ask for a room as far from the casino as possible. The bands ranged from good to excellent. A salsa band played on Thursday night, and we would have gladly paid to hear them.Computer access- in room data lines, in-room TV internet surfing at $9.95/day, or there are three free internet-connected, printer equipped computers in the lobby. They were usually occupied (by kids) till about 10 PM, but if you really need to use one it isn't a problem.Location is convenient, and though across from the airport, there was almost no noise. There is a small strip mall a block away with fast food, a local restaurant, a bakery/coffee shop, and small supermarket. Charlie's Car rental (another excellent value) is less than two blocks away, as is the beach.Security is pretty good- a room card is needed to use the elevators. In general, security seems to be an issue in Puerto Rico. Everywhere we went (not just the cities), there were bars on windows, and walls with barbed/razor wire. Mall parking lots have guard towers (not a bad idea, actually). Another thing to watch out for- parking in Old San Juan is non-existent. After finding the municipal lot filled, I found what I thought was a legal spot near El Morro. It was one of two available spots on the street, no yellow curb, no tickets on other vehices, no signs in sight. You guessed it. Turns out there _was_ a sign, but it was on the wall of a building, not on a sign post, and only at one end of the street. $25 lesson learned. Another warning -fast food isn't. Burger King, 12:30 PM, lunch crowd. One employee taking orders and serving them (at a snail's pace), one employee cooking, one working the drive-thru, and two eating lunch. Took us 45 minutes.Anyway, back to the hotel- the only negative comments I can make about the hotel is that the shower head did not provide the amount water pressure the I like- but almost no hotel does, so that really doesn't count. The other one is that they did not have hair rinse conditioner for my wife, which is strange, as that always seems to be one of those little botlles in the bathroom. Oh well...We would definitely stay there again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great February Vacation My family and I stayed at this hotel last week during school vaction. I had telephoned the manager, whose name is Julian directly (whereby securing a better rate than one I was quoted by reservations at the 800 Hilton number) and he assured me I would be given a nice room. Our suite was #817 which was the top floor and faced the pool. It was very clean and spacious and lacked nothing. The inclusive full breakfast buffet every morning and the 2 hour manager's cocktail reception every evening was great and also lacked nothing. My kids, ages 8 and 9 virtually lived in their beautiful lagoon style pool. The only thing I thought was not that great was their casino. It was super small and had limited slots and two black jack tables. The dealer deals from a deck that is in a black box, so you really can't see whether it's a new shuffle or down to the last cards. THough the minimum bet was only $5, I blew $300 without hardly ever winning (the same goes for the folks playing around me) Any time I did win seemed to bring displeasure from the dealer. The El Yunque forest was very nice, about 1/2 hour drive from hotel. The Canua Caves were amazing, but I would not go again. IT takes 1 1/2 hours to get there, and then you have to sit there for almost two hours before your number is called to hop on one of their trolleys that takes you down into the caves. It seemed very disorganized and you would think it would not be the case, since they've been operating for years. Maybe it's just the time of year where they were more busy than normal? I read another review where someone suggested not going out of the hotel after 10:00 pm. I found this not to be the case at all. There were tons of people walking around at this time and we felt totally safe. All of the locals seemed very friendly, though many cannot speak english (yet here in the states, many jobs require us to know SPANISH...) The strip is very commercialized with McDonalds, Wendys, etc. on every corner. But don't expect fast service from a fast food restaurant. They work at a snail's pace. This is not a bad thing, just different from what most of us Americans are used to. Very few employees can speak english. We went up to a drive through Burger King and ordered a plain hamburger and five piece chicken nugget. Upon leaving the drive through we opened the bag and found 5 ORDERS of chicken nuggets!! All in all, the trip, accomodations, and people were great. Make sure you visit Wyndam El San Juan down the street if you have children. They have a tex mex restauranton the 10th floor with free mechanical bull rides which was a huge hit with kids. Our kids rode it a few times and we didn't even eat there!! Their grounds are also fantastic, but go in through the side door if after 7:00 pm, since their lobby turns into a see and be seen at that time with people dressed to the nines (in their opinion anyway) and you will be turned away if you are dressed casually.Regards!  
<Date>Feb 25, 2005

<Author>jldelia
<Content>Had a great vacation here Our family of 5 just spent a week at the Embassy Suites San Juan and had a very nice time. For an extra $100 or so per night (during what is probably their busiest week of the year) we were able to get adjoining suites, which allowed our teenage girls to sleep in one bedroom which had two double beds, and my wife and I to sleep in the other bedroom which had a king sized bed. Our 9 year old son was very comfortable sleeping on the pullout couch. The rooms were cleaned well every day. A good breakfast buffet was included every morning. There was scrambled eggs, home fries, sausage, bacon, french toast, grits, assorted cereals, pastry, croissants, muffins, fruit (melon, bananas, oranges, pears, apples, etc.), assorted breads, yogurt, assorted juices, milk, american coffee, puerto rican coffee. You could also request cooked-to-order eggs (i.e., various omelets, pancakes). All-in-all a very good selection. When the hotel is crowded they open two breakfast lines, one for those looking for a cooked-to-order breakfast, and the other an express line. This worked out well. From 5:30 - 7:30 every (yes every) evening, there is a manager's reception offering cocktails and snacks (nachos, popcorn, pretzels, etc.). Many guests took advantage of this cocktail hour, but the drinks flowed freely, and we never had to wait more than a few minutes in line for our drinks (you can get two at a time). The Pina Coladas and Strawberry Mararitas were a big hit with the kids (yes, you can get them with or without liquor). I was pleasantly surprised to see they were using brand-name liquor for the cocktails (i.e., Skyy vodka, Cuervo tequila, Don Q rum), okay, maybe not top-shelf, but it was free, and the drinks were made as strong as you wanted. Tipping the bartenders was obviously well received.The pool area was nice and clean, with the exception of the hot-tub. Although the hot tub was clean the first day, I noticed a steady degradation of cleanliness through the week. Although the hotel is very close to the airport, and you can hear and sometimes see airplanes as they approach the airport, I would not say it was troubling at all.The pool bar is only open for a few hours around lunchtime, but the bar a few steps inside the lobby near the casino is open almost all the time, so if you want a drink near the pool you can get one there if the pool bar is closed.The Casino is small,and there are no smoke-free areas. I'm not a gambler so this was not an issue for me, but if I were I would probably spend my time at one of the larger, more glitzy casinos near the beach.** Budget Traveler Tip*** There is a Pueblo Supermarket very near the hotel (well within walking distance). It is extremely clean, and less expensive than the markets near the beach, and obviously much less expensive than the hotel for lunch. Instead of going straight out of the front of the hotel toward the beach, take a right and go down along the side of the hotel toward the thruway. Follow the sidewalk for about 100 yards and you will be in the parking lot. Buy your own beer, wine, liquor, etc. and pour your own cocktails at the pool if you want one before the free manager's reception. This will save you about $5 a drink. The only exclusion around the pool is glass, so buy cans or use cups. Pueblo has a small salad bar, very fresh produce, and a deli (with some hot entrees). They also sell fully cooked chickens for $6 each. Outside of Pueblo there is a Hebrew National hot dog cart where you can get a dog and a drink for $2.The Embassy Grill Restaurant was decent, as hotel restaurants go. The Outback Restaurant was exactly the same as every other Outback, as expected. *** TIP *** Be aware that many restaurants include a gratuity on their bill. It is clearly stated, just make sure you look for it.All-in-all the hotel offered good value and a pleasant stay. Although only a short walk o the beach, those planning on being on the beach every day may prefer to stay at a hotel on the beach itself.

<Author>andrewclauer
<Content>Reasonable price, reliable accommodations I spend two weeks in PR each December for work, with weekends tacked-on at the beginning and end of the trip (thank God for expense reports). I typically stay in the Isla Verde area, for its relative convenience to the airport, and access to expressways out of the San Juan metro area. I've been doing this for the past 6-7 years now, and have stayed at the higher-priced El San Juan and Ritz in the same area, and think that for value-for-the-money standpoint, you can't beat the Embassy Suites. It's 2 blocks from a public beach (admittedly not as spectacular as the private beaches of other resorts) but it has a nice pool area, small but fun little casino and a good 'ole American Outback Steakhouse in the lobby (along with a two small lounge/bars). They also feed you a free buffet breakfast daily, which is not 5-star, but hey, it's free. So after you stuff yourself full of free breakfast, you go nap at the good-sized pool with waterfall and plenty of lounge-areas. Then you go back to your two-room suite (which is at least twice the size of rooms in other hotels in the area) and take a nap on the couch in your living room and watch a movie. Meanwhile your spouse of the kiddies can be doing their own thing in the other room. The hotel lobby is quite pretty, and as with most all Embassy Suites is a full-height atrium affair with tropical plants, palm trees, etc. I've stayed here for the past 4 years, and love it more all the time. They added in-suite (room service) dining for the lazy (or those who have too much work to do, or are too prone to stopping by the casino for 8-10 hours every time they walk by), and the food and service is quite good. Housekeeping is great, and the room is spotless every day. Overall facility maintenance is also pretty good, though my current room could use a coat of paint. The carpeting is plush and clean. The linens are clean and good. I spend more than 100 nights per year in hotels for work (and another 20 for pleasure) and the Embassy Suites Airport in San Juan is pretty high on my list of convenient, and also importantly economically feasible lodging choices anywhere. If you book in advance, rates here are at least $50-$100 per night cheaper than any other comparabe options in the area. For that savings, I'm happy to hop into a cab to go out to Old San Juan or even over to Dorado/Carolina for some night-life. The hotel is also within walking distance of the El San Juan which has a good nightclub and casino, as well as the Ritz and several others. All in all, you can't go wrong in this place for business travel, and frankly I would think it a pretty good choice for family travel too.
